Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey, then thrust the cotton into the ear as we have said in the vein; and if they do not soak in as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proved in the decision of the verse, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, whatever form it may be, so be it.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	1. And let silver or gold be melted into the smallest piercings, and let it flow over; and to press the distillation with a well-made copper instrument, and see if you have the rake and wrap around the end of the cotton; then let your oil or juice gush out, and what you see of your medicines in the case, and the case is in the ear; then blow gently with the rake over all the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or comes from the ear; and it will feel the patient's pain, and so are the distillations I pour into the pot at the same time as I distill in the ear; and keep it from being too cold, for the medicine will not work if it's not hot enough.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the fever of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without having a fever in the ears; and this very same thing happens due to fever or an ear infection, and these fevers never appear in the ear unless one can see; and no time has it ever happened that the pertussis was not visible, and it was seen quite well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The first sentence translates to: "That which comes in front, if it cannot be seen, is a sign of healing in other cases, and in this one, it is necessary to place the ear of the maiden in the sun; look: if you see the apparent inflammation, then the ointment has completely covered this spot of mine.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And also, and continuing forward and backward, if it does not scrape the ear; if the inflammation is of the cheek or neck of the ear, then as long as the char is all on the cheek, use gentle tweezers and a light cope.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the ointment is applied in the ear, then take a soft, light rasping tool and gently scrape it, then put a little fire on it.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the ointment that the malamud sends chills to the ear, gently pierce, and keep your ear's nerves; then put in the ear a tent according to the large pore, and apply some Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not cut the wound as long as the pain is not subsided, or if you put in a tent and moisten it with rose water and powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swelling, then cover the tent with another soft tent made of olive oil and wax, until the swelling goes down; then cure it as soon as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	When the patient feels pain, if a wet sponge is plunged and applied cold, and placed on the ear, and other treatments that stop the dislocation of the joint are used which are treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper charm
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	That which comes from paper is the hair of the head when it is wet and dry, if you extend it with needles and tweezers, and cover it with a piece of gum from its roots; then put it on the scalp.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is not decorticated, if the cautery is a fine cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision is worth its weight; and they are often repaired, and no root suffers from anything; and when they are cauterized by fire, the roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, things come in the form of papers that seem like gravel, and because of this, this disease is called "granule," and it is an assembly of large moisture in the paper and outside; the dislocation is such: take care that the granule does not move on one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make it very wide, then scrape off each part lightly, then take with tweezers, and close.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not feel the paper with your fingers a little, and if it does not hurt the patient; and if the assembly is large, if it is sewn, and the cure is done as long as it is healthy; and if it is small, then do not make too much force, because the restoration will be done gently and carefully.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	1. And if the snowflakes descend towards the ear's lobe to the part above it, and if you reverse the paper, and the snowflakes are placed on forceps, and the paper is pressed from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by incision, it causes no harm; and when the snowflakes are placed, then lift the salty tear oil, and cure the ear that is misaligned as much as the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	2. of the grease of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	3. Exina is a grease that gets stuck in the threads of the paper, and this happens more often with children, and it causes pain to their hairs, and they come to the cathouse in the morning, and cannot see the sun's light because the tears get to their hairs; and for this they lie on their sides, and sleep, and their papers are soaked in moisture that the flesh and appearance have become covered with exina.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the joint with your hand and feel the exertion within it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the wound is if the patient places their head in your hand; and then take a strip of linen, and make a circle according to the quantity contained in each part of the exertion, and place it over the wound; and press with your hands on both sides so that the exertion is assembled within the circle; then make a mileau of the moisture at the sore, trenchant a large furrow, no larger than the wound you make at the healthy vein; and make the skin cover it as much as possible so that you can see the exertion; and in other ways, the exertion comes from the furrow, according to the shape of a greasy pimple.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	1. Pull the hair all around your body with a piece of bedclothes between your two hands, and turn your hands to the right and left as much as possible; and make sure you do not pull on the skin, that you do not touch any part of your body, and do not hurt yourself.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	2. If the hair does not open at the beginning of the shaving, lightly shave a little until it appears; then pull the hair as we have said, and fold the cloth in half and in half, and put it on your arm, and pull gently.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	3. And if such men who cut their hair and put on their heads to make the moisture which is drying more.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the doctor, if he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms at the wound site, and the doctor uses the scalpel gently to avoid causing further pain.
des poilz des papieres	of the paper fibers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper fibers grow unnaturally, and are brushed, they can harm the eyes and cause diseases such as tears and paper mollifications. This is due to the destruction of the hairs. The doctor treats it in four ways: either by burning together with fire, or by medicine according to what is recommended for cauterization, or by cutting and stitching, or by teeth, as I will mention.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	1. It is necessary that you place the main stem of the patient's tooth in your mouth, then turn the paper of the oil to your left hand; if it turns, it is good; if not, then insert an awl into all the holes of the file; and let the margin of the paper or the hair that grows from the hair be on the margin of the paper, and turn the file to the right in your left hand, and then cut off the part that is loose, adjusting the hair evenly, all around the tooth; then remove the file, and place a small piece of silk and thread on the paper, and secure it with a knot, as you see the mirror does, and if it comes out, it should be according to the quantity that you see rising from the paper that is marked with the teeth.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If a part of the body that is skilled at handling paper can handle a great amount of paper according to its condition, then cut all the threads along the two lines you have written, and start with large, sharp scissors; and one of the fringes near the natural hair growth in length, then cut the root at one of the two angles, then scrape the rest; then assemble the two loops on an embroidery needle for every strand of fine thread, and sew the suture, and remove any excess thread from the ends of the silk threads you see, if you do this; and if not, then leave the stitching and threads as is for three or four days; then cure the wound around the stitching with loose, constricting things, because the paper relaxes with the wound and its assembly, but the stitching is dead (as they say the old ones), and it is overwhelming if there is pain; and if in another way: and it is that you see the paper as a figure that is also like the flower of mirth, as we have mentioned, at three incisions, follow the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then comes what exceeds small forces evenly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	Then, if you cannot hold the nails, and the thing is not even, then take a needle or a thread, and cut it to the length of your thumb; and take another thread of about the same length for the large part, and a smaller one for the small part, and assemble the threads evenly between your two hands; then gently press with your hand evenly, and gently sew all the stitches you have made, as we have experienced, then close the wound with suture, and treat it until it is healthy; and if the suture comes to your incision, if the edge is smoothed and the stitching is even; and never has the hair of the paper turned into: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The patient is treated for rabies if it follows this form: and if you convert the paper according to what I said, and then make the snakes by hand, and tie them as tightly as the paper and the threads are long; and hold the heads of the parts you hold the threads; then assemble the two and the other subtly over the paper of the oil, and draw the snakes from the two parts formed; and leave no others, and the leather that is stretched will become rough and wrinkled and torn, as it becomes by it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the patient has enough strength, then treat as soon as possible; and when the wound is healed and the paper is lifted, and no more hair is tied; and this is the form of the two snakes you will make according to this figure and quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	1. The dislocation is such that you need a fine needle, and a piece of silk thread of the same thickness; then assemble the heads and gently pull them apart, and make the ends of the threads as long as possible; then take another fine silk thread and pull the other end, and note the length of the threads; then put the malady's head in your hand; and if the dislocation is not corrected, it is because it is a small dislocation and delicate, then cut the needle all the way through the chase at its root, and make it perceive on the paper as you pull it through the natural hair; then pull the hair until you reach the end of the chase, and cut in the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then pull your hand as the hair comes out all over the chase on the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	1. And if the chase is treated and the hair does not come with it, then when you have ordered the chase to the end of all that you have commanded, as long as the chase comes out with pain and you see it through the vision of the oil; therefore, if you order the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and rises up; and if the hair is short, then accompany it with one long hair from the cheeks naturally, and cut it with the one you let, as long as it is elongated and then lie it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the oil's fat
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati" or oil coming, comes in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes from wounds, or cuts, or burns, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to open the vein is to cut off the suture, and cleanse the lips, and put on linen tents, and leave them as long as they are healthy; and it is only necessary to use in the cure of the veins things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	If you do this, the disease worsens than the first; but the work of things that make something softer, like figs; and the blister of quin or aloe and linen seeds are cooked, and oils are made from none of them, and they envelop a tent, and the cure for this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you give in guard that it does not sound like according to its form before; and these ovraiges that we have said are no better than remedies for this disease, that it does not revive according to its form before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the char that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease called "axacrati" is truly an accident and natural one.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and burns and things similar; and the sight of the shoulder is that if you prick with an needle, if it has two threads, and the thread in the char, and it feels like a left side arm as far as the right, so the needle comes in the head of the shoulder; then the shoulder is at the end of all the needle, and the thread in the wide part of the spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And if the paper is bent according to what it should be, that is good; but if not, then take a ruler and put it in the fire, turn the paper, and make as many furrows as the paper can bear; and let the heads of the angles of the incision you made be like those of a letter that has no "I" grimace; then straighten them according to the quantity of their bentness, which is equal to the amount of the paper it covers, then adjust the other parts, and make them equal in length with a linen thread; then cure as we have said about the mollifying medicines and plasters, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	1. If the disease comes from burning or sewing or cauterization, then it is necessary to remove a simple burn from the hair of the papers, according to what is before; then enter between the two legs of a tent, as I have said; and it must be performed according to the shape of the disease, because it is different in shape, and the skilled masters use various instruments to achieve the return to its natural form; and the disease itself, according to what is necessary to remove and extract in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	2. If the paper is damp, it should be dried.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this cauterization comes to the hands of women in such a way that the paper on it is saturated with oil, and cannot move or perform its natural tasks, then it comes that you cut the point of a razor blade underneath the paper, and lift it up; and the tweezers, as long as you touch what is affected by the subtle spumous exudation, which is neither too much nor too little, so that the patient can suffer from the spumous exudation rather than the oil bleeding; and your incision, which you scratch of that assembly, lightly, so that the paper reforms according to its natural shape; and it is healthy for all that assembly, and never causes any amount of the acrid cold oil, and raises it to the cold sweet oil, and then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and put a fine smooth hair on top of the oil; and after the third day use colsa and other soothing things until it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	The first sentence to translate is "de l’ungle de l’oil". The translation is not
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The first sentence to translate is "Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres". The translation is: "There are two types of the nail: it is nervous and resembles a hard, dry, white skin, and another that is not nervous but resembles wet, moisturized glass that, when touched with iron and cooked with pincer-like tools, does not move; and both types resemble the great enemy, grow quickly, and spread as much as they cover all vision and light and movement of the nail.

The translation is: "And the manner of the incision is that if the surgeon puts his finger in the nail, then he cuts the hairs; and gently place the paper on your hand, then take a pair of tweezers with a small forceps, and hold the nail at the root; then take a needle, and insert the tail of the horse, or of the sheep, or of the beef, and the thread tight; and double the point of the needle a little and the thread pierces through the nail, and tie it with a thread and pull it out at the root, and scrape off all the hair from the nail that extends to the chief, then cut the remaining part in the root of the nail, and leave the natural or broken nail, so that by the incision does not come the tears of the customary; and never has the nail been set at the nail only, and over time, as we have said; then it is scraped all the hair so formed:".

And gently remove the nail, and if you see that it does not move and the reason is that it is pressed, then distill from your mouth into the oil made of lavender and red colies and seal broiet, and extinguish the oil with the other jar; then continue the other incision according to this same work, until it is all done.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the oil, like an abscess, then the milk, and cure first the abscess as soon as it is safe, then continue the incision as before, as long as it is safe.

And if the flesh of the arm appears in the oil at night due to great fatigue, and there is only a part that does not suffer, and tears do not appear; then it distills into the oil that is reddish-colored and made from litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the wood that was pruned
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some people never prune any wood, and they cut the branches and roll them up on paper and twist them into a rose; and if the branches are very thick, then it appears like a balsam tree; and the wound if it is that the surgeon puts his finger in the patient's mouth, then he operates on the wounds, and cuts all this wood as cuttable pieces for the patient, and supports it with force; then make the first cut, and take all of it to the razor until the end, and keep the oil away from the wound; and the incision of a small amount of saporific substance that we have said in the incision of the fingernail and with slight forces of the hand, if it forms after this chapter what we have demonstrated; and when the incision is completed and all the wood is removed, if you use oil of silk or distilled red wine and medicines corrosive, and put it on the wound with a piece of cotton, so that it is secured by stitching; and if it does not require anything, and the hand passes over it, and you doubt aposteme chaut, then leave the oil and cure aposteme chaut with things soothing aposteme chaut; then return to your wound as soon as it is safe, and then make other cuts in the oil by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you heal the care of every weak vein of nature; and of the accidental vein, in the fire of iron; and do not force your hand into any of these fires as long as you see that the member is not affected by that fire.
des voines des eulz	of veins of hairs
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If there are red veins that are covered with oil, and they touch the eye and harm the eye.

Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let each bone be cut in equal degrees according to this form.
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel. de la fistule de l’oil	Of the oil duct
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	If the fistula is called an "arissati" duct: when you treat it with a fire cautery and according to the hot burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not well healed, then it must be opened at the site of the incision, and all the moisture that is in it should be removed, until the wound is clean.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the wound is clean, and you see the corruption and blackening, if all the instruments of this case are made in one form; and it is called an "astringent chief", and should be made firmly at the chief, and should not be pointed like a lime or as it is in the present form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	When you grasp the corrupt bone with your hand, twist it between your two hands, and press your hand firmly until you feel that corruption is removed; and do this as many times as needed, then restore the limb using medicinal ointments.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is seen and cleaned, and the belly wound is seen, and it remains unhealed for more than 40 days, and it does not improve or become septic, and there are no other signs of infection, then follow this method to close the fistula: remove the bone the second time using a hammer and medicinal ointments, and if the wound appears to be healing according to this form, and the head of the bone is at an angle of III degrees, and the fistula is as narrow as possible, then follow these steps as you see:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	1.
