de l’issue de l’oil	1. of the issue of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. When the wound is fully open and there is no drainage from the neck or amauision, if you examine the patient's arm, then the following should be done: first close the wound with a safe seal, then place a ventouse or haterel on it without hurting, then put it on the oil and the one made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then drain the oil, and apply it to the bandages and linen; if the linen is too wet, double each in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the patient has used; then drain the bandages with hard bends, and resume the ventouses without hurting; then tighten the ventouses and leave the oil tightened overnight and in the morning, if you see that it has healed, that is good; if not, then after the day and night, remove the linen and the bandages and the ventouses as long as it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Great dislocation of the eyeball
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a dislocation occurs in the eyeball, it opens and comes out like straw, and one can see inside; therefore, cover your eyes, and with a knife cut into the root of the part that is dislocated, then cut another one where there is a double thread of the part that is looser; and make sure to follow the first cut according to its position, then cut the double thread and take a part of the eyeball, and hold it tightly, then remove the knife and put some ointment on it in a large amount of oil; and leave it as long as the threads cling to the eye, then treat the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed; and never leave the wound uncovered by the eyeball for as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs grow too long, if they are pricked at their base, then hold the eyes steady and do not move until they grow.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil's bag
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease known as "alcunnati" is not other than bags of oil that are assembled in the oil, appearing like a hot descent, and it is not hot; and the manner of the appearance of the dislocation if you make the patient sit at the side and straight, then take the chief between your hands of II parts, and pull the hair as long as you see the bag coming to the desus at your eyes; then it is like a knot, and does not descend and is not combed, and see the maladies things as they were; and if it does not descend, you should know that it is hot, and if the hair comes from the dislocation bag is not assembled as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient between your hands, then take the soft swab and moisten it with the corneal membrane I poc by continuing the conjunctive with the corneal membrane and the cornea, as long as the bow is in; and when it comes out, it should be distilled in the warm water mixed with honey, or hot and fenugreek is boiled and honey, then it should be cured by another remedy until it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearance of the waters in the division, and when it is necessary to cut; if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you place the oil between your two hands, held by the light of the sun, and make the healthy and tightened hair strong; then take the paper of the oil to your left hand where the hairs are on the left, or to your right hand where the hairs are on the right; then take in your right hand, where the hairs are on the right, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, where the hairs are on the left; then place the point of the instrument at the corona through the gristle of a tooth in the blenchor of the oil at the part of least pain; then withdraw the instrument called "almagda" gently, and use your hand as much as it pierces the blenchor of the oil, and feel that almagda enters the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measurement of the almagda hole be at the edge of the measure of the espalance which is of the prunele just before the end of the nose; and this is the corona of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then place the instrument where it has the aigue, then press the hole after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels weak now, if he sees the surgeon in front of him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, and if he feels stronger, open the second vein, insert the forceps with the instrument, and when it is firm and does not move, gently twist your hand a little at a time; then remove a few drops of blood, and cleanse the instrument with this.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a poultice of oil to the wound, or if it is rough, make it smooth with olive oil and plenty of urine, and bind it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Our, and those who are of our kin, put on coats with much bread.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the oil does not enter the wound because of its hardness, as there are too many men with very hard hairs, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctive, and do not pull too hard, but make a small incision, then inject the oil, as we have said; and in the completion of the work, the patient should lie down on his back in the dark room; and should be made to undergo as many movements as possible, with light foods, and without moving his head to the right or left, and according to his disposition, then the patient is placed in this house again, and his eyes are closed, and it is shown that nothing else has been done, but it is necessary to do this before the incision now, but it must be done after the incision, because the swelling rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the patient is in pain, apply oil to the affected area before the seventh day, and follow the instructions of the person who applied the poultice; once calmed, remove the bandage and put on a clean one to cover the wound, and leave it in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then use the house poultice sparingly and gradually increase the amount, and advise that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Then some came from the land of Yrach who told us that in some places they make honey for the winter, but we have not seen it in our land, nor have I ever heard of it in ancient books; and by chance, this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of amalgam, for those who do not know them by sight; and they are truly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And be the head of this very subtlety, and the tail in three angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	of the cheek the nail.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No times are born or grown with different cheeks, and if it has any that seem like scorpions at the mouth of pigs; and if it has such or is enhanced with fox-colored hair, and if it has bone-colored hair.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these cheeks which are not enhanced, and do not grow, it is necessary that you place the patient's face between your hands near the sun; and operate on his nostrils, and graft the horn on those cheeks, and pull them; for this is to ensure that you can hold it steady at the subtle point of a spatula, as long as you can see that the cheek is all one.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, and you examine all the strangers lightly, if it does not cause any harm; and if you do not overdo it, or cause an abscess, if it is malignant, then cauterize as quickly as possible and burn until the bones are charred and the flesh is black and blue or wet and sore.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you do not cause any harm, and moisture comes to the palace, it is good that the patient is healthy; and if moisture penetrates as much as it should, it has caused injury to the bone in the leg, or the strangers cannot be trimmed: therefore it is necessary to cut a piece of linen about a hand's width, and it should be between each nail; and put the thick end of the linen thread through the nail hole as soon as possible, and tie it with odoriferous things as often as it grows out of the nail hole; and many times do this in the child's schools, and it is a light thing for those who see it; then hold the chief that comes through the nail with one hand, and the other chief that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them one after the other as we do with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Do whatever you can to ensure that the child's belly does not become corrupted with this charm, then cut off the boy's penis, draw out the blood, and moisten the boy's penis with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the urethra as before; do this for 3 or more times until all that is left of the charm is corroded; then put a cushion of plaster on some of the jaws for as long as it is healthy, and if you have access to dried herbs, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the child's belly, or when you distill the oils and medicines from it.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or gold, resembling a hanging lamp, like a candelabrum, and you lead it thus; and if you see, if a candle is closed, and it has smooth sides to expel the grease; and it has a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the char and the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times the head of the patient is affected with a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large, until it is seen when looked at; therefore it is necessary to cut at the beginning, and remove all of it, then use the cautery or hot medicine; and if it is delayed as long as it is large, if it is hard, of a dark color, poor sense: if it is not touched by iron because it is enchanted, since no matter how often it is cut, there is always great harm to the patient; and if the enchanted parts are not touched, they are not of iron, and you see that you can cover them, if you see the patient is pale and the malaide is cut, and cure the leu of things that are dry and restrictive.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the joint is cut and crushed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is said that when a solution for continuation comes from one of these cartilages, it does not last long, and it is rare in any man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to see if the wound is fresh at all its base; and then apply two leathers to a frame, and treat it until it is healthy; and if the lips are already inflamed on both sides, then remove all the parts that are sick as they heal, and then assemble the two leathers to a frame, and extract, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and incense burnt; and put the powders on a piece of plaster, or another plaster soaking, and leave it until it is dry, and treat it for the ointment as it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the seam is as follows if you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the seam of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the speeches of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lips of the hands are often hard to speak, resembling grains of sand, and more or less large; therefore, you must turn the lips, and each time you take a nail, and hold it with pliers and press in each part; then use the lemon after cutting the vitriol beads, as long as they are not dried; and then apply the lemon oil, and cure the lemon for dry things as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	Of the horse's knee
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the knee cap has been treated with the horse's knee; what they call the "albulus"; if you can hold it with your fingers, and the bone at its root, and leave the wound or the sinus; then put on the leu vitriole broiet, or other powders that restrain and desiccate; and if the knee cap returns after the incision, and many times it happens, if the bone is second time, and cauterized: if it does not return soon after the cautery; and these are the forms of the estrums for the horse's knee.
des sordens	of soreness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	1. No times are gathered at the tooth's root, where the mouth is between the cheeks, gums that are ill and sharp; and no times is the black and yellow and curved tooth, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and it becomes the blackened tooth. If you must place the tooth between your hands, and its roots are in your holy hand, and you expose the teeth or the gums, as long as there is nothing more; and then I make black and green, and yellow and other discolorations, as they are exposed; and if this is in the first reason, it is good; but if not, it returns to the second day and the tooth, as long as you have everything exposed; and you must know that the teeth have a variety of shapes for grinding, according to what the demonstration shows, because the raser, whose teeth are exposed in other forms than those shown between the teeth, these shapes and others are with you visible.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary that when you treat the patient's tooth pain, you delay as long as possible before eating and drinking, because it should not be hurried; for it is a substance of high juice, therefore there is no excuse for eating or drinking.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is forced to eat or drink, it is necessary that you are certain about the tooth's condition.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain in the patient's tooth has passed, and it is necessary that the tooth be kept clean and the food eaten; and it will not return the pain as long as the tooth is being eaten, because we have already done this for these healthier ones; and when you are certain about the tooth's condition, if it is necessary to scrape the tooth all around the gum; then wash your hands or use small tweezers in the first place and then as many as needed until they are well inserted, then firmly fix the tweezers; and keep the patient's tooth in your mouth between your fingers, and it should be held so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After severing the tooth with a sharp instrument, and if it does not break, then take none of these strings and pull gently on each end, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are felt and drawn out, then it is necessary to fill them with cloth, wherever they are loose; and if the pulling is done subtly with needles, so as not to break the pulled tooth; and it is wise to overturn the girdle to clean the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well aware that you will not break the tooth, and there will remain a part, and it will remain with the patient due to the malice of the root, causing greater pain in the first place.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And you should know that you will not do any harm like those who, through haste and recklessness, break the chariot time and time again, but only cause further damage to what we have known; but they bring it about once by the agony of this great disease, either due to the roots that they sever, or due to the broken chariot that they cut, just as we often want; and if the bone is dry, wash the bone with wine or vinegar and salt; and if they come out of pain and come out, which often happens, use vitriol glass; and if it does not work, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the wisdom teeth, or the first molars, are long and wide with large cusps, which do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large size if they do not break when pulled, and they should be well-made iron, and they should be teeth to hold tightly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth becomes loose when pulled, then you must put your thumb on the cheek side of the socket for one or two hours.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the root is not smooth, then you must remove the tines called "algefris," which are like the beak of a bird; and they should be made in the same way as a lime and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out through all these tines, then you must pull the tooth out entirely from the root, and insert the instrument called "athli", which means "palant", and its shape is like this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be as large as possible if it does not break the bone, and if the root jumps through this, it is good; but if not, then use all the instruments, and the forms come after like this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument with two razors, its shape is like this:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments that are before in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like large tines, its shape is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And so it is that the bone does not break, and the tools are sharp like those of teeth; and also other bones, which are not as strong; and the masters make their instruments subtle by themselves, according to what their hands and the disease demonstrate, because they have some diseases or the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of us, and do not break the bone or other bones, or it is broken, if it seeks as fractures or other bones, or it pits, then you seek as I said, and I help with gestures, of which the form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-held in the bone, so as not to slip, but can hold and open; and then restore the power of the medicine corresponding to this, and if there is any pus in the bone, and it is small, then this instrument can do all.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears to not match the natural course of the body, and its form is ugly, and at the same time in women with sharp teeth, it comes to be that you should cut off the tooth as soon as it appears, and it is not right in the jaw, and it cannot be soaked or polished: therefore cut it off. And if it is growing with the tooth, then use this instrument whose form is like the small beak, and it is sharp and hard like iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And quickly and quickly in the hands, for the hardness of the teeth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears to be like this, then you can limp, if the part of the leg is like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is as hard as the leg of a bird when making nails; and in the leg the teeth are lightly moved in the hands, if it does not move at all, then the end is without any rasping, and the tongue is too thin and it crops the tongue, if it can limp the spicery as much as possible, if it does not crop the tongue and does not corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth loosen by pressure or by chewing, and the patient cannot press on them with their gums where they touch, and you treat them with restraining medicines, and it does not work; if it becomes necessary to bind with a golden thread, because the silver threads turn green and rot, but the gold does not move at all; and if the thread is too thick or too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take a golden thread and a silver thread double between the two healthy teeth, then place the threads between the diseased teeth, as long as you see signs of the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering where you left off, and gently and wisely move your hand until it does not move at all; and if your tie is to the root of the tooth so that it does not escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then fasten the head of the wire to some nails, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put it in so that it does not bend the tongue; and then leave it in so that it is as long as it can be, and if it slips, or the thread comes off, if it is pulled by another thread; if it stays and serves all of its length, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the incisors of the second healthy teeth and the second molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is loose, if it is reset in the gum, repeatedly, as we have said; and it does not become unstable unless it is sharp and painful, and never takes on the shape of a bone of a mare's hoof, and it is placed on the gum where it is lacking, and it is tightened as we have said, and it remains so, and serves all its length:
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Of the copper wire of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is the tongue that comes out of the mouth or naturally; or by accident of wounding; and the wires are such that you make the mouth of the patient open, and it has its head in your hand, and the tongue is relaxed; then cut the nervous wire as wide as possible, until the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if it is hard or knotted, and it is due to pain, if the tooth bites it and cuts it large, and keep the wire so that the fingers do not press too hard, for the artery is out; and when you have done, if the tongue is red and swollen, or cold, then put the lingual nerve on a small piece of linen; and the patient will have a rash every night, that the patient can no longer endure.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the wound becomes infected, if it is not treated with vinegar, then the cauterization at the slow-healing cautery, which is boiled in this way, is done; then the treatment of another kind is carried out as soon as it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound appears to be colored or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, if it is not touched, because it is a gangrene; and if it is declining into a boil, and it has moisture, and it oozes pus, and it is made with a subtle spumous powder, and the discharge is from one side and the other; and if it is not treated in your care, then it is made with vinegar as much as it is infected, and then return to your care as soon as you have treated all parts; then raise the leu of silk and sealant, and the treatment of other treatments as soon as it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the mouth's abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes the gums of the mouth called "godaths", and they are properly the second molars, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not healthy, keep guard: these are hard gums of little sense and fusse color, if not touched with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, if not touched with iron, so for the evacuation of blood; but let it remain as long as it is wounded, and then you will remove it; and if it is of a bluish color and the root is delicate, if you have prepared the instrument with copper, but first look at whether the gums of the mouth are resting and are calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, and his head so be in your hand, and he open the mouth and let the tongue between his fingers, and press the lower lip tight all the instrument, of silver or gold subtle as some needles:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the lower lip all this instrument, and see the abscess, if take the bone and the flesh in the antelope, and drag the tail further than you can; and drag no thing with it, then the cope to the instrument, of silver or gold subtle as some needles, that seems some forces; and all the head is corbeled, and one place another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if it is sharp, then its form is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be trenched on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the hams, if you cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, put hot, warm water on the blade, and keep it clean, and if the blood comes out, if the blade is hot, or if the wounds of green pomegranates are cooked, or if the fuel of mirts are burned, and similar things, until the blade is not stained; then the cure until it is healthy; and never do any other abscesses appear in the mouth than the two hams, if you cut them as you cut the two hams.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with a stomachache that was not passing through the throat, which is to say it was of little sensation; and she had well closed almost all the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the channel that was blocked, and could not swallow or drink, and died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the stomachache was so high that it had been pushed out by two wounds of the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then made a great incision in the one hole, and took out a large portion of the bowels; then I made another incision in the other hole, and opened the mouth and pressed on the tongue; after closing the hole in the stomachache and taking out a piece, and not leaving any suture behind, the woman was able to swallow water and wine, and began to drink again, and continued to cut away at the stomach wound for a long time; the stomach wound closed up, and filled the lower part of the belly that I had made, so that it could not swallow much; therefore I sewed and cauterized the stomach wound: afterwards she began to heal; and I left these parts, and only God can do more after me.
de l’uve	Of the uterus
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the uterus descends to the uterus, and it is elongated and called "perpendicular"; and if it is too large and rounded, it is called "uterus".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the division, and the cure does not benefit much, and you see that the incision of the gallbladder is sutured and made, and it is subtle, then it is appropriate to insert; and that which is rounded and not long; and it is bloody or has the color of blood or black, and it is appropriate to avoid the incision of the bladder.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For it poses great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, as you see, according to the method I have described, of the patient's strength and length, to place the patient facing the sun, and press the tongue on the instrument we have mentioned earlier; then remove the nose, and pull it out, and cut off the two portions that I have mentioned in the incision of the two amandine bones.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut too much beyond the natural end; for if you cut more, it will hurt your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two amandine bones, and cure it as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of pain, then it is necessary that you use an engine for the cauterization of the patient's pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way to cauterize is to make it sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts his head on your hand, and then presses the tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and confirms with sharp, hot iron; and if it is not too thick or too clear, and in using this instrument, the shape is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a hair or puts medicine in his mouth, as the horses do with a bucket, and places the instrument in all the medicine on the eye; and the patient is anxious about his costeit, if the saliva and mucous from his mouth comes out of the medicine, if it does not go to the throat and neck, then hold your hand with all the medicine and press on the eye, as much as you see the relief and the pain of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and pull the instrument out of the cotton in the rope as much as the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five hours or six, if you have skill to restart the cauterization of the medicine, if it resumes, and after cauterizing the discharge enters the eye, wrapped in wool, and clean what is inside the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles as much as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision alone, as it involves cauterization. If it is performed according to this method, take care and use gut, rope, and chamomile and rue and mint and similar herbs, and put them all together or any of them in one pot, and add water, and boil; and it will be well glued with strong earth, and the pot should have the instrument according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and some of the points are inserted into the patient's mouth as much as possible when the vapor rises through the urethra, until the urethra is hardened; after that, it often resumes, until the urethra is dry, and do not make this at the beginning of the onset of gangrene, as many things come later; and do not do this if the onset of gangrene has already occurred.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a needle and sew the corner of the skin with a thread of lead; for the lead thread does not cause much pain to the mouth, as it does not pierce the flesh and is good for the patient's well-being.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened in the throat with a bone or fish spine, or nothing at all; therefore, if you must see what is there, and press the tongue against the instrument until you see the thing; and that which does not open and is stuck in the mouth, it is necessary to make the patient vomit unless the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance, if the thing is removed through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and then wash it with water and then glutinate it; and when it comes to the mouth, if it is rough, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out of what we have said, then take the instrument of piercing according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	1. And let the forceps be placed on the gum if it can more easily enter the mouth, and raise the head; and warn that you do not touch the epigastrium, for all to remain still, nor crush the bone; and it is best that the patient and the instrument hold the device, because it is best or the thing is there; if it is held, or it is drawn further along the entire instrument evenly, as far as it can be.
de la sansue de la gorge	2. of the gum of the mouth
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	3. No time is medicine helpful for the gum, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not profit, then look at the mouth of the patient to the sun, then press the tongue to the device that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the dislocation, if it is all in one small incision, or if there are fine needles that are worth it for this.

des nous	The first sentence to translate is

dou chancre	The first sentence to translate is "dou
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the appearances of a chancre, and it is noted that it must be overcome by medicines, and it is noted that iron must be used for the cure; and we say that the chancre is engraved in the marriage, and great caution must be taken in its cure, and they tell the old man that when chancres are in the body or can be treated if they are like those that are in the mammary glands, and in the fissure, and in the resemblances of them, and it should all be done when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, if not able to approach it, because I have never seen anyone cured; and no one has ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The operation, when it is in the body or can be opened, is that you never purge the patient with black salt; then make it healthier if there is clear fullness, then cut the salt in half to make the operation; then your bones or gums become wet, and all the hair falls out, and the bone of all parts feels nothing left; leave the vein completely empty, and press well with your hand or any thing, and if they dislocate after being cauterized, so that the unstitched parts are not infected; then another cure is needed as soon as it is healthy.
de ydropisie	The first line of the text is "de ydropis
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	The first sentence of the translated text is: "We have said in the division the appearances of edema, and how the assembly of the fever is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure done by medicines, and that which is cured by fire: if it is only; and one should not touch fire in these two appearances: this is to say, tympanites and ophthalmia, because it is a mortal thing; therefore, when you treat the edema appearance called "edema" with medicines, and the cure does not profit, if you see that the patient's condition is weak or if there is another disease than edema, then if you do not touch fire, because it has doubt; and if you see the patient with strong vitality and only edema, and it is not too little or too much, then you should oversee: gently place the patient in your hands, and press the abdomen as far as the neck of the fever, then take the spastemill according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so we proceed with the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And so, proceed with the second part.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a silver snake, and is light or flexible, and in its part closest to the navel, there is one small puncture; and sometimes it costs three, and at other times two, and one; and the head is cut so that it resembles a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes make with the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	And at the head of the sword is the handle, if when it is inserted into the grip, it now comes out of the instrument; empty the part that is most or third, for if you see more than it should be in that hour, by chance if the man's spirit of the weapon has resolved, or he has fainted, or he is approaching death; but according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of his virtue mean, and his pulses; then remove the instrument and hold the grip, and it will be held now by the part that is swelling the puncture that was made at the point, as I have spoken, so that you perceive this manner; then resume the sword the next day, if you see the man suffering thus, and take a small quantity of blood from the grip; do this every day, and keep yourself from fooling as long as it does not matter but a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	1. If you doubt the patient's condition, and they refuse treatment, then the cure for the grave is either burial or sand baths, and perhaps a bath or sunbathing, and it will turn red; and the cure for drying medicines as soon as they are healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after the removal of the boil, just as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	2. of the removal of the tooth
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	3. No child is ever born without having a pustule in the gums, or if it is small, or it is not present in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the patient insists to the point where they cannot perceive anything at all in this manner, according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place the catheter subtly and hold it in place for three to four days or five, and when you see urine coming out, if it is closed, catch the urine and then put it back. And by chance, no one comes out, because the urine that comes out does not leave close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the catheter is small, if it is medicated with a small plug of cloth, as we have said, if it enlarges.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the catheter in their groin are bleak, because no one has ever had a catheter in the head of the penis, because they cannot urinate before they do not lower their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because of this, because the material does not come out at all, and it is a very bad disease.

des pustules de la verge	2. of pustules of the thigh
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. Many times, boils come in the thigh, and it looks like a bad appearance; and among them are malignant and non-malignant; if you prescribe them to be removed at the subcutaneous level, and cut and clean all, then put on cotton wool moistened with Egyptian ointment; then the treatment of ointment diaconticon as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the boil is malignant, of a dark color and suppurating, then you must perform a cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	After you have cauterized it, and the boil is still growing, and has both hair and flesh, then you must remove the part that was hairy; and if it is healing, then the part that was fleshy.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you remove it all together, if you do not feel the head of the boil, and it becomes black and corrupt in the boil, then everything that is black and corrupt must be cut out; then apply honey and flour made from the scraps of grape vinegar and vinegar, and continue the cures as long as it is healthy.

If the wound bleeds, then apply the fire cautery according to this form: it is knowledge, at the stop of blood flow, and at the corruption; and if the head of the thorn is corrupted and retracts, then if you bind or lead the thorn with a cord, and piss the mucus among; and when the thorn arrives at the root of the thorn which has not been circumcised, or has come from a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the instrument broom, as long as the roots are slippery, and release the thorn from the root of all parts; and if this is difficult to do, then scrape the thorn with the spatula of any part of the thorn and the tip; then draw a thin layer of wet linen over the wound, so that it does not get infected.
de la circoncision	The first sentence to translate is "de la circoncision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not less painful than other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will and for the sake of our children, it is the best work that can be done and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not call circumcision their sons' wounds, because they did not use it on their own children, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the greatest part of the masters and physicians who performed circumcisions inside the house, with force, and on all occasions; if it were not for the reason that he has the skill and can do it well, and by chance if he does not have the necessary tools and does not know how to do it.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	When the wound is closed, and there is double pain, and in the mummification, which is not secure at the point of the sore member; and in the mummification of the toe by chance, the iron pierces the vein, and burrows into the flesh, and many times it does not have a proper mummification, and I want it to be.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the mummification which is made with force, all the thread of the line has found its goodness in the experiment, because the forces cut both as well as not.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if it fits perfectly in I all the strength you have; but that the thread is well stretched out on the skin; and that the first dissection is done with the right scissors, if you think the child will understand that you only cut the thread to the verge, and so do it in all the ways you can think of; then cut the thread straight between your hands, and pass the forces between your hands or else between your fingers that the children do not see, and no other strings; then bite your hand on the verge and blow or sneeze, and lift it up as high as the chief of the verge is assembled, then mummify well the dung which is assembled, then tie the end of a double thread, then tie the other line to the double thread, and tie between the two lines, and gently lift the curved part and draw out the knot of the chief of the verge; then leave the sac open and closed, because it is the most beautiful; and sprinkle powder on both and put powdered glue on a moistened piece of cooked pork cut into small cubes, confit with rose oil and fresh, and leave it suspended in the other jar, and the cure is done as long as it is healthy.

dou retenement de l’urine	with careful retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief. The manner of the urine's exit if you take a double cord and tie it at the opening of the linen or cotton, and cut the linen with the thread of the umbilicus; and remove the excess linen and cut it at the umbilicus, then anoint the umbilicus with oil or burt and ointment of urine and urine of beef, and place the patient on the seat, and the vesicle and the verge moistened with oil and olive oil and German thyme; then gently place the urethra in the verge as it comes to the root of the verge, then double the verge towards the boude; then cut the urethra before it reaches the vesicle, and feel the patient come out the empty vesicle, and this is not a good thing according to this order because either you are leading or she will turn; then the thread is all through the linen poc and poc, and the urine follows the linen, then it is drawn out, and the urine is made up; and the urethra resumes as soon as the vesicle is empty and the pain in the patient is alleviated.
des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there is inflammation or blood in the bladder, or when an abscess forms, and you see water and medicines being distilled, then apply this method to all the instrument called "cleyser", and it is shaped like:
