For this reason, do not rush to perceive, but make the patient promise as soon as the pain is soothed; then place the patient on the table, and have two assistants hold him down while you support his back and adjust his limbs to align the leg; let his fingers be expanded, and put his knees against his thighs, and tie them well with a belt; then turn his face towards the left side, and bring the instrument that opens the mouth of the mare, and after that comes the form; it is necessary that when you see this instrument, you fix the first end so as to know the fitting of the mare's mouth, so that what comes through the instrument does not fit more than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if it is larger, it is necessary to cover the fitting of the mare's mouth with cloths, so that the patient is not grieved; and it is necessary that the instrument's handle be placed at the end, and that you draw the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess is opened and it is touched with warm water in the hand, if it covers the head, apply it to the wound; when the bowel is seen, if it is necessary to put shelled ointment in the wound, either in rose oil or green sesame oil; then place the ointment at the edge of the wound, and place it on the wound and the clean, slightly moist puncture point, until the wound is cured; then the doctor will perform two applications every day for two days, as long as it is healthy; never lift the wound and the ointment with a cloth soaked in warm water and honey, and then with warm or roots of lilies and Aristolochia, and then continue the treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	If the wound is treated with the marriage, then it comes that you must not cook with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Childbirth is first in the dance that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see the woman press against the bed, and desire to smell the aroma: therefore hurry the children from further harm; then you should know that these children are according to the natural figure, and they are from your loins, and the second is with him; and when you see these signs, it comes to gently press his belly, so that the child is soon; for when he descends from his head, if it is with the second one, and is monded by the marrriage of its superfluities through good cleanliness; and this that comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes upon its own accord, and comes when the chest or shoulder is hurt, and the hands, or when it comes to the belly or side, and is converted by chance into the collarbone, and through other harmful figures; if it is skilled in the dance and subtle in these things, and warns against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures on how to help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child is born naturally, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her virtues are weak, if it is placed on a stool or by women, and the nature of olive or fenugreek is cooked, and then dance between its two little spatula, which is this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	1. And cut the second one, and hold it against its bone as much as the moisture that is being corrected; and insert the woman's belly as much as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clasp the woman's muscles with fenugreek oil; then apply and suture, and tie her mouth and nose for an hour: if it now delivers the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	2. And if the hands come out, then it is necessary to lightly reset them a little at a time; and if they do not enter, then the woman should sit on the bed, and lift the feet up; then turn the bed over, and sew on the woman, so that she does not fall when standing; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then it is necessary to cut the hands at the corner that is before you, and take out the child, and reset it perfectly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the child's foot that has its toes
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child's foot comes out of its toes, if they can be put on high; and then the nail turns little by little until it is even; then pull the toes and stretch them a little at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	It cannot jump just like that, if it is commanded to, and I make it jump higher; if it fails, let God be blamed.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it cannot jump, as we have said, if the turn is small and small, until it is in accordance with the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For therefore it is lightly done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it cannot jump as we have said, then take a light mace, and oil of sinew, and gum, and broth all in mortar; and make according to the nature of a woman's womb and deflate this treatment, then place it in hot tea until to the ribs; and when it is softened at the ribs, take the collier of iron, and put it on, and leave it an hour; then place it on the seat, then stretch the mouth and the nose, and press the stomach lightly, because the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the issue of the child from its bones
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if it puts its hands on its knees several times; then hangs by its neck, and lets its feet dangle, and then lies down on its belly; and folds its hands several times, and then presses its hands on its stomach, and pushes the knees apart as far as they can go; and if the child does not jump, then catches its feet and bends them, then bends the abdomen forward, then pulls its hands towards it; and makes the child lie down again; and commands the woman to pray as long as the child is like this.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	Of the child's birth that comes out wide with a hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I command the midwife to bring the hand: if she cannot bring it, then I make the woman stand and go; if she cannot go, then I make her sit on the bed and extend her legs; then I relax the muscles that I have mentioned; and if there is no child, then I make her sit on the seat, then study to bring the hand back; and when the child is born naturally, and it is crowning, and I command it to press as much as it can until the child is out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the child's birth at its neck, and its hands spread, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bile stains your hand, then turn it slightly and lightly; when it is equal, if you put the natural oiling of the muscles and oil, as we have said, then command that it moves slightly and slightly; when you have done this, if you make it rest on the side, the command is to press; and the result is that it becomes softer.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way for all the second time.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes in this way for all the second time, if the second time is caught in your nail, as long as the moisture is dry; and if the child can be placed on his face and neck, if the bile flows, it must not be held, and the child will die; then squeeze the child's throat as much as you can, when you have done this in accordance with what is necessary, and command the woman to press no time: therefore, do it gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is said that twins are born many times, and never three or four at once; and this is a strange thing, and few have happened.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and never live long, I know that they are multiplied, and are destroyed by the face which is given them, which is like the bow; and they never issue naturally as all at once, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born gently, if the cure is as we have said, and it is the subtle dance, and made quickly and lightly what it does; and made like that which is worth salutation.
de plusors enfans	Of more children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No children are formed in the marriage of I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more, up to fifteen, and they are all formed as a child by the measure of the glowing sausage, and cover the whole body because by chance it resembles something else, if it is made according to this; if it comes out.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to cut with your hands; if it comes out that the woman is in good health and has no accident or death; if it comes out that the woman is leaned on her back and her shoulders are bent downwards, and her legs raised; and the midwife applies the teign of II parts, or she is laid in bed if she is not treated for the descent of the child;
