if you find the bones in the wrists or in the neck or in the mouth or in the beard or in the chin or in the ears or in the temples or in the hair, and the child is born with its head down, then the bone is in the right hand, and put the cradle between the two fingers of the left hand, and blow lightly with all your hands, and do not forget the bone in any of these places that we have mentioned, as long as it returns to the empty state; and this is the shape of the bone:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then, look for the other bone, or the one you are most familiar with, if the extraction is equal; and then, the joint should move evenly when moving from one side to the other, by applying pressure, and the bones should be held firmly by the teeth, as in this case:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part breaks off, and there are no parts broken on the other side of its two bones, and the other part is pulled; and if it does not break off, then put this bone or the higher one, and do this until all the parts are out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be returned by traction, then it is necessary to wrap around as much as possible, until the whole is out; then the cloth is placed at the joint of the ankle or the knee, and you must do the same with the other hand, and tie the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	When the child's head is large and misshapen, or there is a sudden swelling, if it is necessary to cut between your two hands and remove the swelling; or you will do it with the instrument called "almidach", which comes with the forceps or chaper that follows after this; and then make the child's head naturally large; and then pull out the bones with the tongs, and if the head is forced and crooked, as long as the moisture is not too much, until it is straightened; and if it cannot be straightened, if it is broken in pieces at the mouth that you press; and if it is enlarged at the belly or hips, if it is necessary to cut as much as the moisture allows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is in its mother's womb, if it is the light attraction, and the nourishment is given to the mouth of the pregnant woman.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if the child is in the belly or the pudenda, if it covers that you draw it out gently with your hand; and if the belly or the pudenda, as much as the moisture that it has; and if other members are osteit, and the shoulder is drooping, then the mother's hand comes to the mouth of the pregnant woman, and draws it out; then the foot or feet, and the draw is finished; and if the mouth of the pregnant woman is retreated because of aposteme chaut that has come, then there is no need for traveling, only for managing moist and heavy things; and the management emplaustres, and it is sliced into ague mollifying and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its chest, and you can put it evenly, then as we have said in the living child; and if there is no harm, then the part that should be left is the second one.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the child is misplaced as we have said in the cases of abortion that come; and if the pains come, then if it is kept in a strict diet, and the child is misplaced, then other treatments are needed.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly some children had died, then consulted another of this and was told that death would come to her also.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time came some abscesses in the belly, and inflamed as soon as they were pricked, and began to make great heat.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I thought it would be long, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong astringent with great attraction, and after some hours, more and more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If you thought it was bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted the wound, and with my hands I felt bones as long as the woman got better; and the woman came to me, and it was dislocated a little from the knee; and I did not remember this chapter because when the master made an extraordinary thing, I thought I could help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the dislocation back to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, which is applied to the limbs; and then the head returns to its joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Indeed, the corner should be more subtle and restrictive, and made of a flat or rounded surface; and the mouth should be no wider than the head's diameter, and the margin of the branches should be one and a half palms long and the other half a palm; and these joints should be firmly closed on either side, either half a palm or a little more; and these joints are bent in the mouth of the limb to open when turning the corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	1. Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, can be made of flat or rounded wood, according to the appearance of the nails; and it has two handles, as you see, of a palm's length, and they are wide; and when you open the marsal with all the instruments, if you place the woman's hand on the lap, the pieces and the thighs together in the marsal, and hold the handle of the instrument between your fingers; then use your hand on all the instruments as you did with the nails evenly, according to the amount you see open the mouth of the marsal, until it fits as it was.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all around us, and its appearances are multiplied; and when we see them, the more they are, the faster they work, and the higher they are for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument because you have not seen it, for its needs are not easy to satisfy.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second child is retained in the womb, it comes to your command that you order the midwife to take hold of the hair, and then it is torn from the body, and your hands are forced to the mouth and the nose; and if it jumps for this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, then if I can, and make a poultice or gargle, and put herbs that may open the mouth of the patient, such as mint, rose, anise, chamomile, calamus, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, are either cooked or can be made into a decoction over fire; then put a cloth or gargle that can, and the other part in the mouth of the patient, and let it dry until the vapor reaches the patient; then it is made to be squeezed, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second dose is omitted.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and does not improve, then order the patient to massage their left hand with oil or muslin, and then apply it to the affected area, and repeat as needed. When she finds it, if she presses and extends her fingers gently and evenly, so that the nail does not slip during extraction, but it is recommended to move lightly to the right and left, and then pull. If it comes and becomes distended.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the tooth is very tight, we have called for the treatment of expansion and fumigation with herbs; and if she does not do all that we have said, then keep away from the dentist; but it is likely that what is in the mouth of the tooth, you will tie it to the woman's cooch, then clean it with antiseptic ointment; if it gets better and returns, and comes out; but all the same, when it gets loose, if there is a bad smell from the stomach and mouth, and the dentist is bleached.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it comes to passing fumigations, however, then: no of the ancients have proved fumigation of cresson and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument is made with which the woman is fumed at the retention of flowers and the secondine if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it seems like a dog, and one puts the subtle head on the nature, and the large hairs above the fire; and it is the fumigations with charcoal, and the smoke as much as it is gray, and it resumes another one.
de percier lou fondement	to perceive the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not perceive the foundation, but the one who has understood is a subtle face: if it comes to the dance that he perceives this face at his turn, and does not perceive more of spatumile agut, and garse the plastering that it does not touch; then put on the smooth one in wine and oil, then the care of ointment as much as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not stay in place, if you put or pierce a needle into the skin, and leave it hands free, and it is quick when the children see it going to their rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never has this cautery failed to heal a wound or an abscess; if it comes to be cured, if you treat it, as we have said of the needle in the skin.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula formed by deep moisture
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from deep moisture are nodulated, and grow as fast as those that come from the edges of the fistula or its parts; and when this nodulation is old, it is rough and bloody or subtle, and never are these fistulas permanent; they are known by the fact that they are caused by egestion or ventosity when the patient has egested, and by chance some go in a jump.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that pierce the bladder, and a third of the vagina; and they reach the joint of the cuxe, and a part of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And if you cannot determine the location of the fistula, and it is not present: and you should end your index at the foundation, and cut a thin needle of iron or silver in the fistula when it has no bends.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there are bends, then cut a small tent of plonc or horse hair, as you feel the tent or the hair in your hand; and if you do not feel it, and there is no passage of wind, vomiting, or bleeding, as we have said: be careful that it does not pierce; if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is present in the bladder or urethra, and the urine suddenly flows out, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is present at the joint of the thigh, if it causes the testicle to twist and pain, if it is due to an accident and cannot be cured by rest or medicine; and in these fistulas there is no cure except labor and vanity of those who enter into them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not recent and not ancient, there is hope for health through iron, as I have experienced, and if blood flows from your hands down your back; and you lift your legs up to your thighs, and they are bent towards your belly; then make a tent of rags, or a cloth if it has twists, until you see or the testicle comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	The patient feels pain at the base, if it comes to your attention that you have bitten your thumb or index finger, then it is perceived as a sign; and it should be discovered or felt between your fingers whether it is present or not, therefore pay attention to it; if it cannot be healed, it is not cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is not possible to heal all wounds, but this is rare; and if you can help, then do so, according to the size of the fistula; if it is as said before; and cut through the fistula as much as it reaches the base; and do this twice or three times, as you feel that these charges must be anchored, which are like a penny's tail; then the cure of rough wounds is made, as long as it holds, then the cure of ointment is applied and smeared.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in good health, so be it.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is not in good health, so be it. If he attempts to enter, and cannot penetrate, and between your thumb and index finger there is a thick covering of cloth or soot, and you see the fistula open at this point; if the end of the fistula is at the beginning of the covering, and before the tent, and then cauterize afterward as it comes to the top of the tent; he will be delivered from the tent, and he will be cured. Then make the charms that seem like a pen feather, and there will be none left behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if it does not serve you well, and cuts between you and the wound, whether by fire cauterization or medicinal heat.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauterization has two effects: it is known to secure these loose bones, and to stop the flow of blood and the moisture; then the treatment of soft tissues in the belly or in the groin, as long as the wound bleeds, and the burns are left in place, and the dried plasters are applied to the sores, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	And when it is restored, if it is healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	When a fistula comes to be formed suddenly and is distant from the heart, if it is painful in the belly or fundament, investigate this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and if it is the uterus, or the sac, or the guts, if not it was but a sign of hope and expectation, by the administration of one of the three ways: if you cauterize as we have said, or if you cut it close to the fistula, or if you pull it out and cure as we have said; and do not pull too far forward, if you do not seal the part that holds the foundation, and let the exudations pass through the desired sense; then the cure, as we have said; by chance if it is cured, or you remove that covering and the wound then when it is sealed from the foundation, or by tent or another instrument appointed; then mend the char that is in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to prolong the fistula in the part that is further from the foundation: if it is still a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And no time have pustules been made in this manner: and when you reach the pustule with the tent, it is either costive or founded on a deep cavity of the skin, if you take a tent percée at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I blow it into two, and blow the tent all along the pustule as much as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is persisting in the margin of the deep cavity, then withdraw the fillet from that pustule at its head; and take out the second part of the fillet, and assemble the two heads, and draw them together and leave one free, and do not restrain it again as long as the wires are caught between the two, and touching; then cure the wound as soon as it is sore and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, if you manage to perceive it in all possible ways that you can, it will not be too difficult.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make the fistula through the skin if it can be done, and then the cure, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny thorn, from which the fistula is made if it is long and thin, and on the other hand, not, because one cannot cope with it if one cannot do it, as you see in this:
des emorroydes	of emorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are caused by the foundation, like resin grains, and they have small and large ones, and they are cut off at the root, and they have one or more, and they are defecated from the foundation and the top of the foundation; but those that are defecated are few in moisture, and they are cut off with a little turquoise or a little wine, and they have the color of corns; and the cure of those who have caused the foundation to be defecated is that you command the midwife to let it sweat in chambers as long as the foundations are dry, and when the children appear, and she can catch them with her fingers or keep them in her nails, then she cuts off its roots; and if the uncinate cannot hold the moisture, you should take them to the side, or to the cloth, or to a piece of chamois, and then cut them off, and powder some hot powders that are in the leu of cauterization; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cauterization, so that they are cured by other cures as long as they are healthy; and if the foundations cannot be cut off, you should listerize the midwife with a lister mouth and sharp teeth that can be washed with water, so that it can be cut off openly; and if the midwife's mouth is not prepped, and the stitches are firm from the foundation, then it is the light cure; and if you prepare the midwife's mouth or fingers with the stitches, and then cut them off, and then cure as we have said, so that they are healthy, and they do not fear the incision by fire.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If it comes to pass that you must cut the seam according to this manner: take one thread, thread it through an awl, and then draw the thread through from the other side, and turn the two ends of the other thread over the awl, and if they are wide; and then tighten the thread, then knot it, and draw out the awl, and do the same to the rest, and leave the excess of the sanc at the bottom; then put oil or ointment on the foundation, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to lie down; and then let it be as long as it is tight, and when it is tightened, if the cure for ointment and other cures are sufficient, until it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	The first sentence to translate is: "For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to your attention that you need to resume at the point of a stitch or your nail scratches the skin, which does not allow it to moisten; then the treatment as soon as it is soaked, and if it cannot be soaked, then the cutting resumes more forcefully than before, until it heals, and is burned; then the treatment as soon as it is healthy.
dou fremit	It trembles.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A mosquito is a small appearance that must be present in the chest, and it causes trembling; and no time the fever arises, and it is felt as deadly trembling, and it comes to all the chest, and more than the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that if you take a nail of a goose's foot, or a vulture's claw, and put it on the pulley, as long as the purple circle encircles the pulley entirely; then turn your hand around all the nail as you cover the entire pulley, and place it in front, and draw out the pulley from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, if I make this of a nail of an eagle or iron in this form, and it is subtle and transparent down there:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	You will not see, if you hold the pulley with both hands and press it; and if you see, if the cautery of the pulley is in front or after the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	The form of the fire cautery
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never has it been done to clister with silver or archaut, or fused or hammered gold; and never has it been done to these strums, which are either small or large, according to the size they are obtained.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	When it comes to treating children who are weak and painful, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clitoris is small and large if it is wide, or the belly is shaped in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	If the clitoris has a division or the belly is divided, as you see, and the child's head is perceived, then it may be in one of the costals, and in the other, and the belly may be in a vessel of a beast or of parchment, and all around the small pertus, and between each pertus there must be a space of about an inch, then sew through these pertus with a strong thread, then assemble the belly like a cheese; and when the medicine is given, if it is held by the instrument before a strong thread, then sew; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	1. And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of onion or something similar, then lightly apply the ointment; then the surgeon takes his two hands and assembles them as much as possible, until it is all done, then he removes the splint, and gently supports the patient's legs at the bedside, and if the medicine comes out, as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps a whole night, it will be more help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if you have a dislocation of the abdomen due to disease, and the medicine comes out, if it recurs as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the swelling is either at the base or the gangrene, even if it is as subtle as that of a child; and this is the form of the subtle cystula when it is drawn:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division of the cure of wounds; but you will say the cures of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the instrument or the wound is made, and how it is made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things made by wounds are made of cutting and thrusting, or lance, or spear, or dart, or similar things; or they are made according to the size of the wound, whether it is made at the neck, or at the shoulder, or the chest, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds on the shoulder, because the memory will come to your chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or chief, and the bone is not broken, if it is due to grief of pierce or similar things, and the skull is completely shattered and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of apoplexy: if the same head is healthier than the affected part itself when there is little blood from the wound, and it is healthy on the opposite side; and avoid the physician's fullness with wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not seem healthier, if his flesh is anemic, and does not drink wine, and does not eat meat; and puts the wound, it is best to apply ointment or oil rose only, or steeped in vinegar; and if it has not bled, if it is placed on the wound, it is fresh at all its source, and it is not moved by the air, dust, which I will say a little later; and if it has been moved, if it places some ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	When the wound is large like that of a spearhead and its surrounding skin, and the lips cannot be reassembled by tents, if they can be reassembled by stitching, like I will say for belly wounds, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	When the wound is exposed to the bone, it may be, and only holds by a small piece; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore the hardness in the leather of the thigh, and instruct the patient to eat large amounts of meat, such as testes and cooked flour, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you wound or burn the flesh, and it does not reach the bone, if the burn is total and grows worse, then treat it; and if the artery has been cut in the wound, and it cannot be restrained by medicines, if the artery wants to bleed, and you loosen the cord, if the wound is small, and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put on this powder which smells like the herb that was used.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take a part of incense; mix with three parts of dragon's blood; and three parts of alive chalz, and the fine powder, and apply to the wound, and draw it out as it adheres and joins to all its sanguine; and then it is well if it does not ooze, because one does not want to take the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never has it been done with only chalz, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound has not been moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound is infected, it should be treated immediately with this powder; but add a few digested ointments or flour made from barley and honey, until it becomes soggy; then treat other wounds as necessary when they are healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	When the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, if it is extracted with fine tweezers; and I will tell you more about this later in the bone fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the small wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes of the collarbone and it is simple, and there is no difference between it and the small wound, but if the collarbone is injured or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	1. If it is a nerve, and there is no other remedy than leaving the treatment alone and not putting anything restrictive on it, as nerves draw back; and do not put anything on the wound, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of this is with the brain, which is the colder member; but if the medicine is salve, like cool water washed chalz, and mixed with rose oil, and cucie washed in cool water, and other pierces made in this way, and moistened ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, and the cost and lie of bandages, then the cure as soon as it is sound.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	When the wounds are healed and the skin is full of blisters, if the thorn or lower limb; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes from the wound, if it is treated, and the bandage, and cauterization is done; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the jaw, and the guide is kept, as the meat goes, if the jaw is under the throat's nape, and does not touch the neck but is put back according to its natural figure; then the dislocation is reduced, and some joints are left, then the care of wounds is discarded as soon as it is healthy; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, if it wants; and if there are pieces of bone, if they are cut as much as possible, and those that cannot be cut, if they are left, so that the wound does not become infected and is healed and becomes healthy; and if the wound is fresh, if powder is applied on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has in the wound bone and it has an abscess, then the treatment is as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of the arrow or the spear
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is of the wound of the arrow or the spear, and the wound is gushing blood, then look at the wound's appearance: if it is mortal, then the bone is broken; and if it is not gushing blood, and there is fresh blood all around the vein, then do not delay in applying powder to the wound for the first hour, and do not leave it without applying more powder until it stops bleeding; but if you do not have powder, then apply a mild ointment and lay two cloths on the wound to absorb moisture; and if you do not have an ointment, then put cotton on the wound to soak up moisture, and make the patient lie down on the wound for three or four hours, or more, until the spasms and tremors of the chest are restrained; and when you see the bones in proper position, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	1. Treat the wounds and other injuries as best as possible; and if it cannot be healed, perform surgery with clean tools that have been made; if the treatment is necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	2. If the wound is a cut with a knife or a needle, and it is simple, either on the front or back, if the treatment is done by the surgeon in front; if it is large, use bandages; if it is small, use powder; if it is infected, and the pieces of bone are exposed, if necessary, cut out the pieces of bone; and if they are not exposed, leave the wound open, if the extraction of pus is allowed; and for other wounds on other parts of the body, judge them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation of
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation of "dou derrompement dou ventre" is "great abdominal pain".
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no damage to the intestines, and it is not a difficult matter to set, this is one of the two ways: either by the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is contracted due to inflammation.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is inflamed, you should wash it in this way: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth only, or dip it in hot water and squeeze out the excess, and anoint the intestine as much as it needs to be softened; and never do this without restraining, and it will become soaked and able to be unwound.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the flame depart, if the intestine is rough or sharp and raw, it is because it is inflamed, as this is the cause of the entry of little thing; and if it cannot enter, then a small wound is made with the instrument on the part that is cut, and the first cure is to cut off the size, which is not necessary but must be done in great necessity, and it is the stomach for the tearing: if it cuts deeply into the flesh and does not heal, and then it forms.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	When the wound has grown and the intestine jumps out, if it is reset according to its natural form in its own place, you will have done well, as this is the purpose.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you are able to make the patient lie on their stomach, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then make the head and shoulders higher than the lower abdomen, and thus the wound in the one of the two parts will be higher than the other; and it is necessary to manage this in large and dirty wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you are able to make the patient lie on their stomach, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then make the head and shoulders higher than the lower abdomen, and thus the wound in the one of the two parts will be higher than the other; and it is necessary to manage this in large and dirty wounds.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I pulled out the intestine and it had been 24 hours since it was inserted, and there was a wound of 15 years old, and I cared for it and it became healthy again.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the woman told me that it would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not use any remedies, because there was no medicine to be found, and I poured more on the wound twice a day, and the honey of the bee as much as it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and from the edge of the cloth, pull out the thread as far as the end; when it has been pulled out in straight lines, if the thread is too long or short, or if you have pulled it out on one side and not the other, then pull it out on the other side of the part that was cut; and the stitches will be equal if you do it as the tailor does with the threads, pulling one part and then the other until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, as Galen's method is called, if done correctly, brings together the two ends naturally and applies one end of the needle to the other, in this manner: thread an awl or a needle point near the edge, and make sure that the awl or needle point is close, and leave the two threads of the needle; then turn the awl, and make sure it pierces through the part closest to the density of the stitching, as the threads of the needle; then make sure it pierces through the other part of the stitching, using other needles that are on the other side; and this is the most common method of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	1. If the patient hears this speech and no one testifies, we must cut the belly at the eyes, or as many as there are; and it must be inserted on one side and the other, in the manner of those who are crucified; and when the rupture is near the belly, if it is more painful than the others in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	1. The judgment of the wound is if it is as severe as the judgment of other wounds: and if you treat the fresh wound with all its blood, unless it has moved, then retract the intestine and the gut; then sprinkle powdered char on the wound, and if it has moved, then apply any ointment that is present, as long as the wound bows; then sew the thread, and be careful of the suture, and the mirror; then cure the wound as you would with others, until it is healthy; and if you have no medicines, then use them as much as they come out of the belly, a little fat, and mix it with water twice a day until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other skill in other cases than treating wounds; and if you doubt that the wound is not serious as to members, then it comes that you lightly oil the chalor or rose oil on the wound, and put on bandages and gauzes; and if there is pain or rash on the skin, and many times it comes, if the rash is cleaned with red wine, and also the rash comes to the intestine; and the percussion is made, and the guts are found, which are large, then it is lighter to cure than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The first line of the text translates to: "The intestine that is called 'young' cannot heal until it is opened, and this is due to the sensitivity of the wounds it has, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the horn jumps from the wound, and it is reset as the intestine is, while it is fresh; and if it becomes infected and turns black, then you must remove the black leu that has become infected, because it has veins and arteries; then cut through what is between the ligaments, and pull the head of the horn away from the wound until the extraction is done when the horn jumps, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, if it can be restored in several places, because I have seen that some were healed or the belly of a lance; and it was the wound on the left side of the stomach, and it became an ulcer and fistula, and therein was the egestion and vomiting; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not stop subtleizing until it was healthy, and I observed the signs.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when it was sutured, I doubted that the patient had not suffered in his belly; but he had no pain, but lay in better conditions, and drank and ate; and they told me that when there is a small wound in the intestine, one must stitch it in this way: first make large incisions, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the mouth has overturned, put it in between the lips, if it draws the mouth back; then close the teste, and it holds if it cannot slip, then make another movement in the same way as before, until the wound is entirely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	1. If the tip of the intestine is burned and causes no harm to the patient, and it can be tied with a very fine thread that is coated on the intestine of an animal, in a similar manner: take the tip of this thread of intestine that is free from moisture, and then tie it to the tip of this fil line of silk thread, and then pass the thread through the needle, and then sew the intestine, and then pull the thread tight; and this way of stitching is not better than according to the path of love and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, if it does not heal or become healthy, it should be tied with a very fine and delicate tie.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It is said that all wounds and abscesses, when they heal, if they are called universally "fistula", and likewise if they are hairy and have a thin covering.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the saying of the nodation that is hard and painful, or one does not feel pain, and is as hairy as the tail of an ox; and never clear-skinned, and sometimes thick, and never sparse, and never thin; and I have seen this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and has no pain, is only due to one of the eight causes: it is to know, by a little pain or corrosive, or because of its malice, or because it has too much bowel, or because it is porous and the matter is of poor quality, or because the medicine is not good in the cure, or because the corruption is like pestilence, or because of the property in the region is slow digestion, and slow health, and runs naturally; or one has wounds or bones: and I have shown all these causes and their signs and remedies with medicines in the division.

Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	1. If the patient has a fiancé whose hair is falling out and the baldness is not yet visible, and the hair is dark in color, if the baldness worsens, treat the patient with Egyptian medicine that has been made: take oils, perfumes, and linseed, and place them in a pot over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take according to your need and make it into an infusion and a honey mixture, and apply it to the breasts and tighten the wound, and leave the medicine on for two hours, then draw it out by gently squeezing; repeat this process until the breasts are restored and the pain is gone, and no candles are used made of grapevine and ashes, but only honey and wine, which have the property of cleansing and washing; if the patient cannot bear the candling, or the Egyptian medicine does not heal the wound, or there is little ointment left, then apply a mixture of ointments and wine to the breasts and wound, or a mixture of various ointments and ointments that have been prepared; if the wound is too large, so that the leu or the candling can enter, and if the wound is discharging pus, then apply a mixture of Egyptian medicine or basilicon ointment to the wound.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the belly is in its proper place, do not let it be disjointed; and if you do not cover the wound with something as you see fit, but appear to be doing it in such a way that the belly is at the lowest part of the body where it is, since when the belly is in its proper place, do not let it be disjointed and if you do not cover the wound with something as you see fit, but appear to be doing it in such a way that the belly is at the lowest part of the body where it is, then take consolidating medicines to help put the patient back together, and put them on the side of the belly that covers all of the patient; then cover the wound with something as you see fit, but make sure it is not too tight in one place and too loose in another, according to the amount of the wound, and put it on the wound of the sick part to align the belly, and do not forget to adjust the great dressing later once; and the person who is by the wound of the sick part often feels the belly, whether it is venom or little or much, or digested or undigested, and take care if the patient feels pain or no pain, and if it has happened to him or not, and when your medicine has been extended and you see the nature that jumps out of the wound of the sick part, if you think that the breasts have already swelled, and approach the plague; then leave the morning or evening, and when you clean the wound, if you change the dressing and reapply the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts become wet and indigestible after a long journey, it is said that the breasts do not lactate.
