de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is an abscess that develops from the tip of the finger or toe, or sometimes from other parts; when it becomes inflamed, and is not cared for, if the abscess opens, and bursts and oozes blood as far as the root of the finger, and in some cases even the entire root, and then comes the corrosions, which reach the bone, as soon as pain sets in, and the head is large, and the color is changed.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, then you must cut off all the excess that has been removed from the finger, then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The cauterization is a great help when the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the finger, and it starts to prick, and burn, then you must cut off the part of the nail that points at the finger, and pull it up, and apply some subtle and gentle medicines on the remaining part of the nail, then treat the wound as needed until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	2. And if the corrosion is in the bone, then it should be removed as soon as possible, because as much of the bone becomes corrupted and affected, so much less it can heal; and if you see the bone corroding, then cut it off at the point where it was said, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is hard, then cut it off, and it will feel great pain, then cut off the nail as soon as possible, and warded that the cut does not go through the finger which is of the nail, because the patient will feel too much pain; and if it happens, then put something that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the crushed hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The crushed hand of some men by chance is very painful, and by chance it may be broken in parts, and never united, and no one is born with the root of the joint, or the birth is not in any of us.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are crushed in no part are not silent, and those who are crushed at the joint are silent; the size of the one who is crushed is lighter, in the same way: size it in its root like a wide saddle.

In the event that one wishes to reduce from the rear, if it is possible for you to first cover the hand around the bone firmly, then cover the bone with a suitable cloth, and then treat it as soon as it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The signs that come are either born or caused by wounding, or caused by burning, or by other things.

des vils	of evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	There are large, bloated veins full of melancholic superfluities that come to more and more members of the corpse; and more come in the legs of those who go to prayer and work and bear.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must never administer any purge of colic, and then the proper of the basilicon.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is on the hot spots, and the other is to draw out the black blood; and the other way is when you tie the vein, and you draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	1. de la voinne civile	of the common vein.

This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may grow elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from the flesh that comes from the hide of the snake, as it comes from the belly of the snake and turns, it grows between the hide and the char.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante. des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that are born between leather and skin.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our country "disease of beef" because it often occurs with many wounds, and is a small worm that passes between leather and skin, and goes up and down the entire body, and is felt well at every joint of the limb, as soon as the hide comes off or it is cut, and jumps; and it is caused by the excrement of some humors, like worms, serpents, and squiggles, and ascaris; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes up and down the body, it reaches the head, and comes to the oil, by chance returns, and destroys the oil; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the patient healing and drawing in, if it can only be that when he will: if it comes to pass that you see the leg of him and from the opposite side well tightly, then cut off and take out, and put him in the cart, and do not worry, if the cauterization by fire is done as it dies; and the greatest harm it does, if it is that it goes into the oil, as we have said; and if you see him coming or going near the oil, if he is strained from it the hair forms, then cut off, and take out; and it is necessary to use the cauterant with mundification of liquid medicines for the humors of men, and avoid the flesh of enjambed animals as food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from dislocation
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "wakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that affects certain members, and spreads from member to member; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a female patient, and I saw my arm, and saw a small flesh in the vein of her arm; and later, I saw it rise as quickly as anything, as if it were living silver when it cut through the other; the pain left that arm and moved to the shoulder, and then it spread throughout the body, so that it came to the other arm; then she told me that she dislocated her shoulder, just like you see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was surprised to see how it moved from limb to limb, as I have never wanted this disease to occur in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I wanted to ensure that the pain was not transferred from one limb to another, but I did not want this. I thought it was because the woman had tight muscles, and the veins were exposed, and because of this, the constraint appeared; but I did not know if this was true for those who are delicate, and have moist veins and recovered bones.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see the curing of this disease, and the patient feels pain, does it open as we have said, if the limbs are tightly bound and untied, and then press on it as long as the constraint remains at the joint; and cauterize the joint; and if you do not see it with your eyes, if the cure of those who have this constraint is like pills bitter and pills of rue, and similar ones.
des saiettes	The first sentence is "des saiettes".
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The second sentence is "Les saiettes sont diverses, selon leur semblance et selon les leurs dou cors ou elles chient." which translates to "Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the strength of the nerves or they shoot.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The third sentence is "Li diversitez de lor est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres." which translates to "The diversity of them is that they have those with large points, and small, and hooks, and soles; and those with angles, and those with tails, and those without pieces; and one that dislocates in any member in different ways: or in the principle member, it chevies like the brain, the liver, the spleen, the lungs, the heart, the stomach, the bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. If you see that you are going to have to extract this arrow, because death will follow in other places; and if the wound does not appear to be deep, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then remove it, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of a broken bone is when the arrow pierces the bone and causes the eye to jump, and the person who is near the eye falls to the ground, and they have loss of sight, and confusion and despair and trembling and pain in the limbs, and inflammation and pain in the tongue, and spasm and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of cold; and by chance it is without nose or ears; and by chance affects the speech and voice; and a sudden jump of the wound, white like snot, resembling a gout; and if you see this sign, if you hold on to the care, and remove the arrow if it is not deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it pains or throbs is that it hurts or aches near the medial side, and it feels as if it is cracking in something hard, without emptying; and by chance, the shoulder also becomes stiff, and in the cold, there is cold sweat, and sinks: then the signs of death begin to appear.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the eye that has not opened is that there are no signs of swelling from the wound, and the throat is bloated, and the face turns pale, and gasps for breath high up in the chest, and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	When the shoulder is dislocated and the chest is covered, if it is tightened on the small ribs; and there is great pain and suffering and gasping; and all the members of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the dislocated shoulder or stomach, by chance, jumps from the wound, nothing indigestible of the meat is left.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the dislocated shoulder or abdomen, and in a sudden jump through the small intestine, if there is no hope in the treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the dislocated shoulder or bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out in a sudden flow, and the patient feels great pain: signs that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and neck and shoulder and arm and elbow and spine of the back and fingers and toes, and the member seeming, are saved according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the flesh or artery, and it is not visible, as I will tell you if I know, because you are doing this.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to me once a shaft hit me in the shoulder: I tried it, and from another part of the grease of the ear, it was saved without any difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And there came to him a arrow that he fell into the fat of the oil of oils and the paper of oils, and the arrow was reponed, and it could not reach but only to the tip of the point, and it was the arrow great like a Turkish arch, with no weight on his ears; the wound was safe and he did not come near any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens. Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And a arrow was found in the man's side, which he thought was mortal; and then after 30 days, if it did not change its position, I cut near the arrow, sewn it up, and the dislocation followed, and there was no further complication.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if a man has an arrow in his side or back, and it causes a wound to bleed; and the arrow remains in the wound, and does not change its natural position, and does not find any harm in any of its natural works.

Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	A member of the royal household had a dislocation in the shoulder, which was previously stable but became unstable over time. It was then realigned three years later.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is widely stretched.

Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	The patient's shoulder is judged to be unable to restore the cartilage of the nose: I will restore it therefore, and it was relieved by the wound, and it became healthy for the patient entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have said the quality of extracting some arrows, if you apply your care according to what I will not say, for the books cannot make everything appear completely pure; but the masters of the art can manage well with a few good things and what is present and lacking, they perform nine operations and use nine instruments, as things that are extracted by this art descend.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from the limbs or they are not broken because of two ways: either by the hand or they enter, or in another way; and the one that is thrown through or it enters, is an arrow that has entered into the flesh, and it has never been thrown once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, if she leaves it as is, and it becomes inflamed and the issue comes out; and then she gets stuck in the bone, and she cannot come out if she leaves any parts empty, and then she jumps, and if she does not jump, if she perceives subtly at all times, as long as the issue is made sharp, and then it comes out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrowhead gets stuck in the bone of the shoulder, and it goes towards one of the chest cavities, or any of the accidents I have mentioned to the assistant: if she does not remove it, but leaves it as is until it becomes swollen after some time, because if she removes it, it will cause death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	When the joint is not dislocated only in the bone and does not cause any problem, and there are no other accidents, then the patient can move freely without pain.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the joint becomes dislocated and cannot be reduced, then apply firm pressure on the affected area as I have mentioned earlier; then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the joint is not visible and cannot be felt, then try to locate it using any available means; if you feel it, if there is no instrument to use, and if you do not want to cause further pain or injury to the wound, then gently pull on the arrow until the wound is as large as possible; then remove the arrow from the joint, and if there are ears in the joint, then break or crush them as much as possible before removing them; be careful not to break the joint.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not once, if the leaf until it is read, then the hair, for the extraction is painful.

And if the healing does not correspond to the wound, then the cure in this chapter is wrong; and you will be cut on the nerve and vein, and made to hold the incision with your hand, and treat the arrow as if it were the most serious injury that you have had, and if you do not, then follow what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or it opens no thing of him, or the skin is tight in some place where one can see or feel it: then cut it as much as the nails can take, and then pull it out: if it hurts now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if your hand turns around as it enters the bone, and widens the bone, then it will be withdrawn.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction. des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are common veins, of which the healthy ones are thirty-one, of which sixteen are the two "herbage" arteries that follow the ears, called the "aspires"; and the vein that is in the temples; and the veins that are in the front of the head, called the "aspires"; and the vein that is at the top of the head; and the veins that are in the chin; and the veins that are in the corners of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the veins that are at the bottom of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	1. The veins that are commonly found in each arm are usually five: one is the cranial, which is on the western side of the chest, and it is called the "grief vein"; and the other is called the "fast" and is composed of the cranial and the basilic, and they call it the "grief of the shoulder"; and the basilic is when it is on the eastern side of the chest, and they call it the "grief of the belly", and it is under the femoral, and it is the one that is usually found, which opens clearly under the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	2. The salvage is the vein that is between the auricular and the anal, if it rains; and in the leg and on the thigh are three veins: one is the "grief" of the pocket of the western side of the chest, and the second is the "grief" of the ankle of the eastern side of the chest; and the vein that is called "nise", which is in the ankle of the other thigh; and in the other leg there are three veins of the same kind.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	1. The ears that follow the eyes if aided by old catharses and migrations; and the quality of this saver, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the malady of the patient, and rub the ear or the ears that are of a rough cloth; then stretch the patient's neck to a vine, until the ears appear behind the eyes in the dependent dependence of the head: if you want to do this for your child, and you feel the pain in your child's head, then take the lancet, and cut through the vein just above the bone, then gently hold all the vein with both hands, and cover and the skin and the vein well until it is completely healed, and make sure the sutures are as you see; then tie and lie down, until it is healthy; and I have already said the incision and the cauterization of the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	1. The health of the two arteries in the temples, if they are old, hardened, and customary, and if they are affected by the tears of the eyes; and if the physician qualifies them as I say: and it is that the physician draws his collar as much as the eyes open widely; and it feels like the touch of cold water on your skin, and then it becomes sensitive; then he should gently press on the cheek above your index finger, and remove the lancet, and gently lift the cheek above, and the eye, as you have done in the other cheeks, and make a cut according to your necessity; then release the physician, and put your hand on the cheek for an hour, then put cotton; and then form the wound, and leave it as long as it is healthy; and we have spoken and of their extraction and their removal, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The patient with the vein of the front of the head is as sick as the crown of the head with ancient diseases of the face, and migraines, and bruising; and you should examine it if the patient tightens his neck by twisting it as much as the vein appears; then take the instrument called the "fissure", which is shaped like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and firmly with your hand or another thing, and let the blood come out according to the amount you see; then loosen the collar for the patient as much as possible, and hold the vein so that it is safe and never twist it with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	All that is needed to heal the wound is for the flame not to be too hot; and through it, because the bone is near, and by chance, the fire breaks the skin when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The healing of the two wounds that are in the two arms if they help the bones, and the elbow, and the bruise, and the face in the oil, and the diseases of the face; and the quality of their healing if it is that the maltreated pulls his neck with twisting any ligament, as before; then the healing, and so the healing of a long wound, a little wide and a little large flame, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance very sharp; then make a large incision as much as you can, and then lift the skin, and hold it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	If the wound of the vein is not deep and does not seem to be infected, or if it is a skin disease, and rash comes into the skin, and especially when it is old; and if the quality of the wound is that the flesh clings to the collar, then hold the wound in your left hand and take the subtle flame short, and touch the eyeball with the flame between the two eyes, because the vein does not open well, and now it will start to burn; and do not let it burn too much, and make a large incision as you need to, then close it at night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	1. The patient's health is aided in the prevention of diseases, at the beginning of medicine, and in many afflictions, and infections, and corrosions, and herpes, and ulcers; and the quality of the patient's health is estimated if the midwife tightly holds the neck of the child on both sides, as we have said; and the midwife being at the loins of the midwife, and the midwife sitting at the siege, then the vein is made long, and wide, and then the blood is let out in large amounts, or as much as possible; then another part is done on the other vein, then the limbs are loosened, and the veins are straightened, so that the midwife does not tighten; and it is left until the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the hares
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the hares is aided by the veins of their lips if they help to close in the mouth, and the corruption of the genitals, and gums of the lips, and teeth and jaws.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is if it is made to sit before you, and holds its neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, of which one is on the left side and the other on the right, and they are black due to their dark color and because they have thin dark veins: therefore, do both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then take the largest one from each part, and do all the veins that are open and closed, as it is a different method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the health of the tongue, the language
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are dislocated from the tongue if helped after the health of the head, and it is at the gorge's extreme, and diseases of the throat, and diseases of the mouth; and you judge the quality as soon as the patient's hands are before the sun, and loosens the tongue, and looks at each side of a black vein: healthy on one and the other, and do not alarm too much, for they are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that are commonly healthy are in two ways: either by pricking at all the flame with wide fingers, or olive oil subtle as you cut, and they are called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and extremity of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire cautery is such that it is called the "mouth" when it is newly made, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is made to open the veins with flat hairy stones that contain large blood clots and are troubled; and this is the form of the fire cautery:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle to apply, and it is safer for the veins, or if there is subtle blood clots.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The benefit of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is that it helps with diseases that are low in the throat, and neck, and belly, and artery, which is also low. And it is necessary for the physician to make wise decisions and avoid the artery that is low.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If the artery is pricked and blood comes out, if it is necessary to stop the bleeding, as I have said; and it should not be pricked with fire, but cut with a knife as I have said.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the basin does not open obviously, if it is necessary to force it, and change another one; or you do not want any rain on it, or you are in the vein of the arm: it opens obviously; and the fire is extinguished with a knife, as I have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the vein of the wound, if it is necessary to force the arm, and touch the vein as much as you can see the pulse; then sign the vein with a knife, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with fire anesil; and watch that you do not hurt the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If you see coming out from the top like the urine of a child, and it is red and subtle, you should know that it is not from the artery: hurry to you, and put your hand far away, then watch your hand as it comes out without staining, many times; hold your arm, let it go, and do not move the muscles; and so be careful, and do not move it until it is healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	2. If it is not stained and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, then if the artery is open, because the end of the return; it will become stained.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	1. Take a scalpel, sharpen it, and then take one of the halves and tie it well to the other; if it is not slippery, it is good; if not, then use the poultices that make it non-slip; the poultices are not greasy in other positions for the small wound of the wound, and the pain of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	1. The health of the vein is improved if it is treated with blood when it is infected, and when it is inflamed, because it is composed of basilican and cephalic, as we have said; and it should be washed with the nerve that is inflamed, and if it does not become too much in a short time, and it opens the nerve, and it becomes fat and healthy, and by chance it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open any holes for its subtlety, then it should be cleaned with the instrument we have; and remove the nerve from your body.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If blood flows between the two veins, if they are long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The salve for the head if it helps, that it attracts blood from the chief and helps the wounds; and it is safer when pricked with olive oil or myrrh, because it is the most safe of all wounds, because it does not harm the nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	All in all, it is best to use it lighter the first time, and do not hurt anyone, and then continue; and by chance, it may cause some discomfort in some people, but it does not hurt anyone the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about health is that it is to maintain health and avoid diseases coming; and it should be made in one of the three veins: it is to know, the head, fast, and basilic; and it must be done at the beginning of the patient's arrival, and again during the night or the next day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The health that is amiss with diseases has no determined age, but when it comes to eating or drinking, in all hours and at all times; and it does not matter if it's for children up to 14 years old, or women who are only carrying for four months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They should not neglect their health at all, even if they have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when one becomes healthier, in whatever way that may be, if it causes the intestines of a light cyst to expand, if it has no need for feces retained, and if the wombs do not have superfluous harmful intestines, nor too much meat or yeast, even if it is caused by colic, vomiting, and abdominal discomfort, and multiplied by women's menstruation and labor, and sleep, and breakfast, and whatever virtue, or by the arm or a bruised corse; then subtly the humors are reduced, if it is not too large, by meat and drink and medicines, as you can afford; then take a bath, nothing harms you, to reduce your sickness, and to cleanse the veins before the third, as we have said; and keep away from work, and pleasure, and luxury, and such things; and be modest and humble, and so be healthier than those who are sick, and rub your hands twice or three times, then draw out the nails if they are too tight or small, as you cannot remove them without; then rub the hands with ointment, then put your right hand on the swollen vein a little oil, then take your left hand and put it on the swollen vein as much as it needs to be squeezed, so that the vein does not bleed or hurt.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords to the healthier part, and if they are too many, then when one is placed on the fire, it withdraws from the fire, and cannot open the vein, and then it is one of those; and if the vein is opened, then it is the wound too tight, for then it comes to the healthier part, and the healthier part must be advised in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; but if not, then it returns a little more of that joint or suddenly, and if it is not enlarged, it is not good.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	1. If the patient is small and the joint is swollen, and the shoulder does not move much, and there are no abscesses on the arm: by chance, apostemes come; do not enter or bathe, then resume the treatment as it pleases; and if the wound is small, or the subcutaneous tissue is not cut too much, and you doubt that there is not so much blood as you have seen, because of this in the same wound at all times; and the work is done quickly, otherwise if the shoulder is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	2. If the shoulder is swollen and you do not resume the treatment, and put a little oil on it, because it lightens the corse of the pain, and makes it less bitter in this shoulder that the oil lies; and afterwards, give oil to the shoulder that you have oiled the wounds, to strengthen the course of the pain; and it itself makes triaicle and bowe d'eus, when you put it on the shoulder; if subtly it does not cut or part when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	When large abscesses appear, which often come multiple times, if it is not healthy only once when the vein opening is small, if you hurry, and put a damp sponge on the wound and wrap it in a cloth, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if there is no black or greenish discharge at the wound after several days, if you do not know why; and if you see, put nothing on the wound except aloe or mint cream, or a similar substance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is gangrene and appearance of the health of the basilica: then place your hand on it, and if you feel the shoulder move with the compression of your hand, that is the appearance of malformation.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	However, you must not place anything on it that we have said, for by chance in the cut without the artery; but I applied it dry to strengthen the shoulder, then another care, until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And apply each sac according to its quantity of virtue and color of the sac.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black when it comes out, leave it until it is red; and if you see it large, leave it until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, leave it cooler.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	1. It is necessary for those who are in pain and fear, and have the skill of extracting blood, to make a larger incision, and widen the wound; and for those who are weak, the opposite is done, and it is made safer and more often, and it should be made safer by cutting across, not touching; and this way of healing is saved from the dislocation of blood and nerve compression, and it is worth noting that the longer incision is not wider.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	1. And for the one whose heart needs healing, it is necessary to give a moistened piece of pomegranate juice; if it is cold, three times or four times as much blood; and if it is of a cold complexion, before the moistened piece of pomegranate juice, either in honey or aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and well-odored honey.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If the patient feels ill after the evacuation of blood, if he sweats and has a putrid odor, and uses other things as we have mentioned in the division or chapter of sincope for the evacuation of wind.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If the patient sees his arm swell and become sicker again, if it happens when he is weakened by great sickness, so that he becomes sick little by little, according to the amount of his virtue continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If the patient sees his arm swell after the first illness and is strong, if he becomes sick seven hours after the first illness, or after the second hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if it seems healthier from another point of view, then it should be healthier to do it the next day or the following one.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has to have blood from the body that has been scratched, and brings on fever; if it comes out in large quantities, and opens the wound as much as it can; then that you reward all the conditions of health, and put your hand on the wound every time it gets healthier, so that the death does not come from pus, and this happens many times when the healthy ones are negligent; and it will be enough to see that your arm sweats, and let the sang run the second time, and the wound is closed, so that you press on it; but if it is swollen, then stretch your arm as quickly as possible, because it would be harmful; but leave it as long as it gets healthier the second time; or if you do not touch the tip of the flame, until the part that has been scratched freezes in the vein and is put back into the fire, and gently press on it with your little finger.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, then let it be and do not hold it tight, as long as the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to draw blood again, then if the vein is in the same arm or in another arm, or in another hand.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy because it is composed of the same material as the vein from which the blood was drawn.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way of the healthy one is that if the patient's hand becomes red and hot when blood is drawn, then it is tied tightly until the vein appears well, then the blood is now passed through the vein, not too wide or too long; and the wounds are large and well placed near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be stopped, then the hand is made hot again and the sang is left in the vein as much as possible; and if this is the case, then do not tie the hand in hot water, because it is put in more than necessary; and the vein from this one is safer than all others, because it has not been pricked or cut.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	1. If the salve of the right hand saves from all diseases of the belly, then this is the way: wash the hand, and dry it with hot water, as long as the vein is open, if you can; and if the hand is clean throughout, and does not cause any harm; and do not let it remain too long, for the skin is dry and prone to cracking, and then put the hand back in hot water, if it does not freeze in the wound, and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	2. And when you have treated as much blood as is suitable for your task, if you put on the vein oil and seal it tightly, and then make a small hole in each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The patient's hand if it is affected by the disease of the mouse, and I do everything as I have said to the left.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The health of the sophene if it is beneficial to all diseases that are caused by the heart, such as heart diseases, and retention of flowers, and gallbladder disease, and knee and hip diseases, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his health if it is that the patient has fever and sweating as long as the vein is cold, and pressing on the joint of the puncture; and the vein if it is at the ankle, and by pressing the puncture wound to the knee; thus, the rain is healthy, or larger than the ankle, or at the knee, which is needed.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cleanse the wound with your clean hands, if there are nerves that are exposed, and the wound is long, as in cutting; and let the sutures be tight.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound does not come out, then set the wound in a sling and let the wound dry well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound becomes infected again, the second time it is due to a small amount of fluid; do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and then make a poultice of the other wound properly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The inflammation of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of the foot, and its cure is the pain of the heel, when it is due to a sac.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	1. And the quality of its health if it is that the patient has caught or bathed, and draws on the ankle IV times in twisting, because otherwise it will not open the vein; and if it opens, then the healthy in all ways you can, and across; and it is worth coping, for the lesion is safe and it is returned to the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	1. And if you do not coping, then the healthy no one who has opened or down from the joint that has opened or side little two, and turn the small door; and make as much blood as you see, and then let go of the link, and put on cotton and draw; it is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	Of childbirth pains
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horn, or iron, or wood; and ventouses can be done in two ways: either by cutting and pulling out the blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventouse, which is made by cutting, can be done in two ways: either it is all fire, or it is fire; and ventouse which is made by cutting and blood extraction is made in twelve degrees of the heart, of which some are at the top, and the others in the chest; and the others in the collarbone; and the others in the shoulder blades; and the ventouse of the chin; and the ventouse of the elbows; and the ventouse of the knees; and the ventouse of the ankles; and the ventouse of the toes; and this ventouse does not take any blood, only small wounds that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not cause much pain, as we do with childbirth pains; and it only needs to be kept clean, neither hot nor cold, in no disease that comes from repletion, as long as the heart is dry.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessary for illness, or by habit, if the midwife comes every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and also in the middle; for there are some who, when they have to ventilate, weigh a lot; and if such as have accumulation and bruising in their face, and in their chin, and at the collar, and are pale; and those who have a fever in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and spit out blood; and if it is some who cough, and see only blood, and feel pain; then there are some who have such that they sweat, and their heart beats fast, and they die.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it has been one month, we command our patient to rest after three hours a day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The health of the head helps to alleviate pain in the child... that comes with these wounds, and it is only after all the blood has been evacuated; and this rest is beneficial for the health of the pediatric patient, and only those who have a cold complexion or are sick should use it, as it can cause great harm; and therefore, only the watchman in use, or those who have cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal, if they become dependent, and for this it is necessary to put the ventouse in a smaller place due to fear of dependence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventouse in the neck is in the lower part of the shoulder and the throat, and for this it is necessary to use it in emergencies, and to remove the bowel from the abdomen, and for all, and to relieve; and it should be tightened, as it holds too firmly, causing dependence or stomach and intestines.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventouse in the neck is around the collarbone, and it causes pain in the shoulder, and obtains and migraines, and causes strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in the lower part of the throat; and it is necessary that you command the patient to express his hand when putting it on, that he does not cut the artery, and does not cause dependence.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The first line of the text translates to: "If the wind causes the cheek to swell, it is a sign of disease in the mouth, and corruption in the genitals, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; it is also a sign of sickness in the upper lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The second line of the text translates to: "If the swelling of the shoulder indicates disease that comes from chills and filling, it is a sign of illness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The third line of the text translates to: "If the swelling of the cheek is as great as three swellings in the arm, it attracts blood from these large swellings; and instruct the patient not to press too hard, because the swelling is naked and knows how to decrease and narrow arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The first line of the text translates to: "The vacuum that is used at the crown if it is too large can cause headaches and other diseases, and it must be large enough to have a good hold; otherwise, it may break; and it causes great pain.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The second line of the text translates to: "The vacuums for the legs are healthy when they open widely, as they attract blood from all parts of the body, and relieve old pains from the knees, thighs, and bladder, and stimulate the growth of hair; and they are in the use of the second phalanges and second metacarpals, and they weaken the body after long use, and cause palpitation in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	1. The manner to apply the cautery is if you first empty it, and then do so successfully, and move it evenly, and continue doing this until you see the red and swollen part, and the appearance of painful blood; then stop, and put back the cauteries, and take care in the positioning of the cors, as there are those who have such tightness and loose parts: if you only want to injure once, and make large wounds, and a few punctures; and lightly apply it.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	2. And if it is not big enough, then if you only injure once: the first time by making the vein's passage slightly larger.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the head is not treated immediately, it can be seriously injured; and when we only need to draw a little blood, we only need to do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we need to draw a lot of blood, we often return; and if the head is not treated immediately, it can be seriously injured; and if the pain is not noticed, and it ends when the ears are perceived slightly, and for those with thick skin and hard bones, and who have rough hair, you should apply ointments of cooking oil: if this is the case, use olive oil, or sweet almond oil, or sesame seed oil; and if it is silver, use garden cress oil, or lemon oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar substances.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	When the swelling is large and cold, if you take oil of almonds, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	When the skin is thin and large pores, it is not recommended to apply oil, but it is recommended to wash after the application of rose water, or cold water, or mushroom water, or onion vinegar, or porcelain vinegar, or other similar substances.
