Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And that which has moisture, if it rises from sweat, or rose water, and mint, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive superfluities rise from wine vile, or from ague of sweat, or from decoction of anet or chamomile, or from other similar things; and they do not become healthier by ventilating before bathing, but after the bath, an hour or two; and they do not sleep after ventilating, and they must wake up when it is time to ventilate and when it is ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And when those who are healthy become weak and too hot, and they sweat excessively and burn, if they consume cold things like pomes grenates and endives and laitues in the salad, and similar things; and they drink pucins, and char of chastron, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Here comes the translation:
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	1. The incisions that are made to cause pain are those that are made on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and bowels and intestines and bladder, for this member does not suffer from sharp pain unless it is drawn out by drawing blood from member to member, as we do with the breasts when they are not sick; to relieve the viscosity that is in the member, as we do with the stomach and bowels to alleviate the member; and to relieve the pain when it is inflamed or pierced, if it is relieved by its own virtue attracting inflammation, or if it is left without inflammation; and then it is made when it is placed on the liver and spleen when it has retained inflammation, and these incisions are administered empty to suck only; and never are they administered together with fire, and never are they made with cold tea, as in some diseases of the plague, and in this way we fill the incision with hot water, or with water that has been cooked herbs, as it is.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is as follows: It consists of two strips of palm half an inch wide and a small perforation at the end of each strip, similar to a needle, and a loop of wire or iron to be inserted before to prevent it from piercing the patient's member; and in the middle, a hole of wire or iron to receive a thong, and according to the disease and weight of those who take them, whether they are thin or fat. For the vacuums of children are different from those of adults, and smaller than those of the obese.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	1. And it must be placed on the dressing on the member: take the candle or the liniment, and insert it into the wound through the hole that is in the wound, so that the linament is at the bottom of the wound and does not burn the patient; then place it on the member, and you must place it on the abscess as we have said, if you see, if there is vapor coming out, and if you open the wound; and take the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	1. In the wound, however, that is infected with the disease of catarrh, without any hole or abscess, and is not infected unless it is clear of fever, and is only placed on the member when it is clear of fever, and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	1. Withouts are not made except in parts where there is no way to put on stockings due to their small size, such as the lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in these parts, if they are without stockings like a char's, or if they are not, and other similar cases; and the quality of the user is that when you find withouts that are in soft waters, such as they are, take them and put them in a soft water bath, as long as they are suitable for the family and have nothing in the belly; then it is healthy for the vein and the wound, then clean the member as much as it is red, and put on the stockings; and when they are flat and smooth, if it is possible to put on the wound, put it on, because this is after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the leg of the wound, and then the edge; and if you see it too late after the corset of the gauze is removed, then take a piece of linen cold water, and put it on, as long as the gauze is not soaked; and if the gauze is multiplied, then put on vitrol or gashes, and similar things, as long as it is soaked; or you can make half of your legs with cut-off nails, and leave them as they are on the leg, if it is now stitched; and if you have more time, then take others gauze.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the wounds do not take on the salve, if you rub the lesion with warm ointment or thread it as much as it needs, and then put it on, and as they feel the soreness, if they become red; and when you see that they start to heal, if you dust a little aloe and silk or charcoal, or dust, now they will.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book on wounds.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of wounds and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	I advise you, young man, that if you do not follow this chapter, you will never see any of the ancient books, nor write anything; and for this reason, the science is neglected in our land, because I have never found a book on the subject; and I do not know if there is any, except by the science of the ancient books, or by my studying them and treating the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and summarized at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the dislocations that are done, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the sum of words and chapters or sentences where the meaning can be understood, and more so if those who have experienced it learn this noble art, and learn to teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that if any injury, dislocation, or twisting, or tightening comes to no part of the patient's body, if nothing harms him on either side, whether it be from the weakness of his limbs, or from the weakness of his bones; or if he is not very thin, or too fat; and if he drinks not cold water, nor drinks any fatty drinks, nor eats very little, nor eats too much, and does not fill his veins with blood, until he has no doubt of gangrene or expansion of matter in the member; if he returns to his former state of health as soon as he can.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the patient's meat that causes large swelling, or if it has viscosity, like wheat cooked in vinegar, and tests, and peas, and pancakes made of wool, and eggs, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the swelling that is regained, it returns less quickly than the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that the broken bones and cracks cannot be well recovered or strengthened according to their nature by the care of the members, nor those that are too flexible, like those of small children; but if it is necessary, reset the broken bone with large tendons that are united with the member as it was before, and do not leave it without its work, and for this reason it is necessary to avoid large amounts of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And observe that fractures come in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the leg or foot, and I will explain all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go in one direction and others in another, like the size of a pen's tip.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a small notch.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each fracture has its own way and instrument for restoration, according to what remembrance comes to the patient's mind; and the fracture of the bone is due to it being twisted, and open well by depression, and some pressure on the hand; and if it is not tortuosity or fissure, but there is no fracture, then there is no tortuosity or fissure; but there may be twisting or fissure or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move it with your hand alone, but use the medicines that will come later, and then attempt to pull it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Examine the fracture that will occur in the bone, and the two parts that are disjointed. It is now necessary to align them as evenly as possible, without causing any pain or swelling; if the swelling subsides and comes out, then leave it alone until the swelling has subsided. Then move it gently and carefully, and consider whether the restoration of the bone is lighter than the restorations made on other bones with pieces missing. Then attempt to pull it now.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone of the foot, if it is broken into two parts, if it is hands or fingers, or a part of your hand is small members, or two tendons, or one tendon and your hand; and set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are adjusted, if you adjust by your own hands the additions in their place on the muscle that you push, and keep that by your effort does not cause the surgical wound or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels good to the hand if it seems that it is not well: if it curves beautifully, and does not strain too much, do not press as they do who come by their own effort, ache and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the limb is at rest, if the patient carefully keeps it still, neither by day nor by night, nor when turning, nor in any other way, then the limb will be well secured so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For if he feels no pain, unless it is at rest, then it is necessary to put the limb in proper position so that it does not feel any pain; and keep it straight, so that twisting does not occur when it is repositioned; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I will tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It is said that broken bones are of different kinds in small and large size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For it has large limbs, if like branches and leaves: if they are covered with fine linen and subtle threads; and those that are thick, if like timbers and beams: if they are covered with a wide and hard cord, for the wide ones embrace all the great member, and draw it evenly by all parts, unless there is no tail; then the end of the threads is light and three or four times the size of the member, and the hand is tightly held around all the thread, then go to the break and draw it less than the break, so that the break does not extend much part of the healthy part, then take another thread and turn the end right against the broken part; then return to the part opposite the break, and draw it gently, neither too much nor too little, as we have said in the first part of the break; then put between the threads covered with linen or silk, as it is even, then tie everything with a bend, and then put your good nails on, if there is no gape or burst.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it is inflamed or gangrenous, if one puts on something soothing for gangrene, and that stops the inflammation, and leaves no traces; then one must tightly hold one's breath, and they should be of about a wide rope's length without sagging, or of fist-sized pieces of wood, or of palm fiber, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	However, it is necessary that the piece put on the wound be larger and wider than the others; and should also be as long as the member is small or large; then tightly hold the eyes as you did in the first part, then tie a thread around it as you did in the first part, until it is as tight as possible, and do not stretch it too much; and the thread must be clean, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen the works of fools who make their wrists with linen threads, it is a great mistake, for the wound cannot be held tightly if it is too fine, and it only serves to make each eye smaller than necessary.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is guided by the shoulder bones after the scar is removed in healthy people, if they put on thin linen or silk, if it does not crack.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splint, and the bone is broken, I will tell you the treatment for this after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is said that it is difficult to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not possible to straighten them immediately after the fracture; rather, it takes several days or weeks, depending on the severity of the injury; and this is how the ancient methods of restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists were done: take flour that is between the millstones, mix it with a lot of water, and make a dough with it, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way to restore breaks in various positions, as well as for women and children, because it is neither too hard nor too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	1. Another way to mend fractures and dislocations and twists: take barley and linen and unguent and Arabian gum and mugatel, in the ratio of X to V; then grind and add aloe, in the ratio of VIIII to V; and make a powder, and mix it with the dough of urine; if the complexion of the face is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	1. Another way to mend twists: take Arabian gum and vismud, in the ratio of X to V; grind and add aloe, in the ratio of VIIII to VI; cinnamon, in the amount of X; arsenic, in the amount of X; then dry well, and cook with water or urine, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to mark joints and bones is to use oils and liniments that soothe the pain and reduce inflammation. To make these remedies, mix fresh mint with cooked oil and honey, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore health, but they are useful for soothing inflammation and relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another remedy for healing broken bones is to make a poultice using dried figs and earth oven bread, and apply it to the affected area.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another remedy for healing bone fractures and reducing inflammation is to make a poultice using dried figs and earth oven bread, and apply it to the affected area.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	The root of vismallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of violets, and each part; and boil, and conserve with wine, and wash the limbs with moistened coriander or lavender water, or plain water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to apply the ointment more frequently than the first, when the abscess is firm and comes to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Boil the roots of vismallow, and linseed meal, bay leaves, honey, and all the flowers of violets and chamomile, each part; and boil, and preserve with salted or sweet water, or wine, according to the chalor of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that one should not put anything on the broken bone to restore its strength, as only wax and oil are needed, and nothing more. He says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It appears that Galen suggests putting on the broken bone to restore its strength, with dry things like honey, aloes, and incense, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to relieve pain and injury: take mugath and chevon's hooves, or oyster pins, and vismalve, and seil, and the bones, and make a plaster and apply it to the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the pain gradually subsides, and one takes care that the patient does not feel any pain in their joints or bones; if it does not subside by hand pressure, and pain or itching comes to the joint, and you hasten to remove it, and cleanse the wound with salted water, and plunge in cold water, and lift the leg as much as the itching ceases and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moistened with water or rose oil, and wrap in a bandage as long as you are sure of no gangrene, and allow the inflammation in the member to subside, and the pain to cease, then resume the gentle pressure, and a little emplaustre, and do not strain it too much; and gradually as it becomes healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the wound is gushing blood, bleeding, and painful, and the swelling is increasing, then you have skill in plastering and bandaging, if it recurs, as you have done initially well.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if you do not see any sign of what we have said, if it does not bleed for more than three or four or seven days; and never more than twenty days, as long as the wound is suppurating and approaches the limb to the char sus; then the restraint should be greater than before, and the flesh will grow larger, as I have said before; and if you see it becoming drier than it should, be careful that no pus comes in; take care of the wound with hot poultices each time you clean it, and every day; thus, you will cut off the pus from the limb, and mend what the flesh has done, so that the limb does not become distorted: this is harmful, and if it is not cared for properly, and I know of no other way than to wash with warm water and dry it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounds
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of wounds exist, and various shapes; for there are wounds made by the blow of a spear, and the bone is broken all through the bone, as if it were made by a hack or a fist; and therefore this kind of wound is called "hacking" wound.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	The spear breaks the bone through different senses of feeling, and this kind of wound is called "absolute" wound; and these are the wounds of these two great or small gashes.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a percussion wound, or a cut or a piercing of the bone, or a piercing through the bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a continuous fracture, which approaches the tissue that is exposed to the bone or it is under the bone, and this wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If the wound is repaired in the bone as well as subtly as possible, and it is a small cut, and for this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by injuring the pierce, or by tearing, or by something seeming, and it lets the piece of the bone enter, and it is the same as when they burned the caustics when they were applying them to the burners; if it enters through the pierce.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let's examine all types of fractures by the methods used on them, and through the corrupted chart that is used.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the capital fracture is known by the fact that when the bone is discovered and touched, if the dark fracture is not open, it does not seem to be a capital fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care not to harm the patient, and if you see no other accident, such as vomiting of clear fluid, admission of understanding, extension, and pain, and fever, and the nails turning white and red, and other similar symptoms that cannot be cured with doubt, then...
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unexpected accident, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the first pain comes to you, and it is in the shoulder, then it is necessary to rest the bone before the fourth day at night that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is like this, then if you rest the bone before the ninth day, unless the cloth of the bone is corrupted, and the accident that we have mentioned comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes close to the cloth that covers the skull, then it is necessary to cut the broken part off: and it is that you cut off the head of the wounded patient, and uncover all the ways that you can, and reveal the wound in all its aspects, and if blood comes out, or pus, help him with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with oiled flax; and rest the wound as long as the pus is stopped and secured from dislocation; then start to heal the bone, and it is done according to two methods of treatment: one method is that you cut at the end that is narrow, and it is in this form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he cuts another piece, larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many different sizes of blades, some thin and others wide, and they are sharp, and are made of iron; and you shape them gently so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and brittle, then you must perforate it with a drill, otherwise you should sharpen the blades with files, and do not make them too large, so that they do not go beyond the end of the bone; and you must have a margin or circle around the point that does not pass over the bone; and you must have more files, if each time you drill, as long as the bone holds up to your test; and this is the form of the three methods of files:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	1. The quality to assess the fractured bone is that you put wet cloth on the bone, and turn it over your two hands until you feel that the bone is perceived; then take the cloth away a little later, and then do everything else, and cut as incisions in the bone that is between the holes, and do it as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, as you trace the bone with your hand, or with any of the traps that you have like needles, pincers; and keep away from the brain and the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and cut the bone, if it covers the wound that is made in the bone by any other instrument resembling an incisor, but it should be more fine and subtle than the other incisor; and if it does not make any small bones or scales, if the light bones are slightly scratched with the traps; then cure the wound with tents and bandages that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of opening is when it is said by the Galenic method, which is more accurate; and the force is very great, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, the fracture opening being exposed, so that once you have discovered this part, you will measure from the center of this incisional lenticular chief, and its form is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the part is broken in two layers, if the cutting is towards the bone; then firmly press with a small maillet, so that you lightly touch the entire bone, and be well prepared for the thread that is opposite; if it is near the bone, if the bone is lightly touched, because it is sensitive to injury, and causes pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only covered by soft tissues, and it has small pieces, then cover those sharp edges with the subtle rasp that you must have several quantities of, to smooth out each bone according to its size and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you start with a coarse rasp and then switch to a more subtle one, and continue doing this until it is well-smoothed out.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair removal and subtle fracture treatments, you must adjust according to its address; and this is something that cannot be undone by the one who studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	1. If the dislocation is discovered, it comes to light that you must preheat the linen according to the size of the wound, and apply olive oil, then place another doubled bandage, such as II or III, and apply vinegar and olive oil, then place it over the first bandage; and do this more gently so as not to burn the face, then administer through other linen, and do not strain it too much, and leave it for one or two hours until the inflammation is calmed, then remove it and administer medicines such as roots of these plants, flour, powdered incense, aristolochum, and similar things; and from these things make a powder and place it over the wound and administer further medicines without burning; and wait until the wound is clean, so that you do not leave the ointment or assemble boils, because when boils assemble on the skin, they can cause great harm to the patient, as they can cause the malaise to spread widely; because when something mordant is placed on the face, it causes pain.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	When there is no accident that happens to the patient, if we have said so, then it is doubtful whether there is any doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no darkness comes forth except by medicine that has been given, then some virtue has, if you apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and one part of glue, and mix it with water, and it is applied in various ways of cures until it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Wise men say that the two parts of the nose are never broken, or only one, for they are bones; and this is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut the small toe or index finger and make the break even with the natural shape of the nail; and do this lightly, and let the patient feel no pain through your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the part of the nail, and cannot be reached by the toe, then you should put it even with the tip of a thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is in the second part, then you should repeat this and restore the first toe; if not, after the ninth or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then cut the tip of the index finger at an angle, if the break is in a certain place.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	1. If you cut at another part, it will be; and the wounds are so large that they fill the cavities with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	2. And no restorer will say that one must smoothen the wounds in burrs, and each day dies.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	3. It seems to me that it is well, but they must be smoothed in the making of oven ash and bone powder; then leave the wound, as long as the bone is hard and the cartilage becomes strong.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	4. And never cut on the neck of the wound, and if it is soft and hangs down, and holds the thread, and smoothes the pain; or do what you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the wound is infected, come to the physician as soon as you can, for if you put on linen or cotton that is oiled with rose oil or in a vessel of digitalis, it will help.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is not infected, if you put on ointment made of flour of sulfur and incense powder, mixed with fresh eggs, then put on light sponges, and do not close the wound; and if the wound is small, and it is torn into small pieces, if it can be closed with stitches, then cut the stitches, and treat the wound with antiseptic ointments and powders, as well as able to close with stitches or bandages; and if there is no pain in the wound, then treat it with compresses and put on needles, until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated, there is no cut, and the fracture is not severe, only slightly so, and not broken into pieces, but rather crushed like a nut, if you understand, lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, to place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, then place your index finger on the right hand, gently press the fracture, and hold it with the other hand, and fix it.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	If the fracture of the lower jaw is healed in two parts, and it is equal, then you must administer extension to both parts.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If the teeth move or break, and they are pulled by gold, silver, or silk threads, then tie them around the broken lower jaw, and put on two large sheets; and put one of the sheets on the jaw, and tie it with a well-made nail or a piece of leather that fits the jaw, and tell the patient to rest, and feed him light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, and it moves to another place, and then put it back in its original position; and apply plaster of Paris with a lot of urine or flour of sieves, after you have set the broken jaw; and apply a light coating of plaster, and let it dry, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; three times it will be healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If the abscess bursts, then it is best to follow the instructions given earlier.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If there is a fracture and a wound in the same place, treat it as a simple bone fracture. If the break is not severe, it can be treated at home.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is wide, enlarge it according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have all the bones in place and there is no pain, if the wound is wide, make sure it is clean and apply bandages as needed to prevent infection. Make sure the wound is dry before applying the bandage.
de la forcele	From the force of
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks more often in front of the shoulder, towards the elbow, and the break is in three ways: it is broken and disconnected in two, and it has pieces, and it is the lighter one to restore; or it is a broken one with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the opening is when the break is with wound, if you have two assistants, that one paints the dislocated shoulder with the force of the break; and the other extends your collar towards the part; then place the break equal on both sides, so it forms as it should, and there should be no appearance or inequality.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have further experience, then place the shoulder blade of the patient at a distance from the body with a round or flat object, depending on the size according to your needs; and hold it firmly but gently in your hand so that you can even out the fracture as necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you do not wish to treat the head of the force with defense, because it comes from behind, then it may cause the patient's hatred to rise, and place the shoulder blade at a distance from the head, and bind the shoulder blade with the hair, as long as the bone of the force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two, and if you find the fragments, it may be that you sell them; and take care of the lighter pieces, and if the bone does not join by any means with any part, if it is to one of the incisions you have made; but you should remove the force of this instrument for safety's sake.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not too sharp, and should be as large as it can be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the wrist; and if there are two, if you see, and one is wide, and the others are narrow, if it is the swelling of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of aposteme chaut, if the wound is large, or if you doubt aposteme chaut, if you use the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if apoplexy comes suddenly, if many are in the olive oil and wine and vine, and they put it on.

And the fracture of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is to put oil on the bone and apply a poultice of powdered milling and oak ash, and light sponge rolls, and a small drill at the fracture site; then take a large palm frond, then double the sponge rolls over the poultice, and press it; then take a fine needle of three to four inches long and long, and wrap it around the palm frond so that the bark remains; and put the needle on the fracture site, and turn the palm frond under the bark, and soak the clean bone in clean water, and soak the dirty bone in dirty water; and tighten each part, and when you see that the bark holds the sponge roll, and you see clearly that the needle does not stick to the bone brake, if the reward is for each jorn, and when the patient sleeps, if the restraint; and make the malady lie on his back, and he puts it when he wakes up a small orillier of oil on the bone, and raises the helper to his head; if the fracture is strengthened by the alignment of the shoulder blade, or by tying the arm to the collar, and does not slip out of hand due to accident, just XX jors; then resume the application, if you see that it has merit, and draw it and leave it as it is, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most XXVIII jors, and less in no man.

de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the upper and lower "humerus," with one being larger and the other smaller, and the larger one is the head, which forms the shoulder; and the other is smaller, and is the neck, leading to the smaller one. By chance, only the larger humerus or the smaller one is broken, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light and the cure; but when the large ones are broken, it is often a poor cure, and more painful than when they were broken individually.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bones are broken, it is best to gently extend and put them evenly.
