Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the head in its place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, then he puts each in its place, and if there are none that point out how to put it back, and you cannot restore it in its place, then follow our advice and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken to the single cauterizer; if he takes care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration there are post-operative swellings, then make a poultice of oil of rose and wax blanc, neither too hard nor too soft, and gently wrap it around, as long as the swelling is appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then he cuts the bone, and puts the powder of the mill with a lot of urine on it, puts the plasters, and makes the cuff larger than the others; and he checks if there are VI plasters or arms in more positions: whether the cuff is in one of the bones, or in two; and pulls it more from the cuff that is closest, and less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and the powders that are under the cuff, which are wet and not too hard or rough, and the threads, whose ends are drawn out, are neither too long nor too short, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, if you must warm the member with hot water as much as necessary until the itching is relieved; then let the member rest in its place.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the stretching, and if the limbs are softened and the bones are loosened, and it seems so, then proceed.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the wounds do not come to the member because it is too tight, because of which you must soften the member as much as possible, and let it rest for some time until the wounds heal, and then stretch it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If these things do not come to the patient, if they do not loosen the joint for twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If the patient is not found, then the hands can be placed on his collarbone, and it should be even; and the collarbone should be settled with movement and adjustment, and it should sleep on its side; and it is hoped that this fracture is restored in XXX years or XXXV, and by chance in XX years, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the wrist fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Hoping that on the back of the hand and in the wrist there are few fractures, and it only twists many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	When the plant of the hand is broken or crushed, if the patient feels pain, and immediately stands straight in front of him evenly; then place the hand on the extended leg, extend the fingers of the broken bones, and put them evenly in the holes as they are well joined; then apply plaster and stitches, if necessary, then put a splint according to the amount of the leg; and wrap it in a fold of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	If the fracture is at the side of the abdomen of the plant, then make a sleeve of cloth, and instruct the patient to wrap it around their broken plant; then stretch from a long sleeve, and let it be as large as the plant of the hand, and stretch it, if it is possible.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the elbow, then it comes to pass that you place a splint on and another in the plant, if the hand is overstretched and straight, then the arm is completely tied, and the line is firm between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture does not come to any of the two, if it is bent, then it should be tied equally; and the elbow is lifted with the plant, and if you see that a splint is placed right and small for raising the fracture, and does not move; and if the fracture is in other parts, such as the index or one of the others, if it is bent, and the hand is held tightly, or a splint is placed on the healthy finger that follows; or you tie them all together, according to what is appropriate, or you place a splint on the plant, as I have said; and take care in restoration and disposition of the aperture chisel, and attend to what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken bone
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the shoulder is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward; the restoration is if it is possible to rejoin the fibers of the fracture, and the other one is left.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient groans when he looks at his face, and then extends each muscle of his limb evenly; and it is when the fracture is removed from the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the shoulder, then one or more of the muscles turn away from the point of impact, and the others are pulled back by the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And when it has reached the groin, and then separate the ligaments of the groin, and stretch the extension; then place the bone equal to its two hands, as it is according to its natural figure, and then place the template, and the socket, and the joint, does not move if it comes.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it has been strained, if it is left to be soothed then return to your work and your care; the wound is made in part like this.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the knee with a bandage I bend double in II or III, and remove the surplus, then bend the leg as much as the heel comes to the root of the nail, and place one string between the thigh and the leg, loosen the groin of the bandage, and turn the leg and the thigh back the bender; then turn the leg and the thigh back the bender, then put the bandage on the knee, and put an estee on the bone of the knee; then place the lee vuit between the knee and the thigh to make the strap equal to the knee and thigh, and start to tie for form III or IV on the bandage; and as more you add to the bandage, and less the tightens; then take out II strings that you have tied between the knee and the thigh, and the III estee that are on, and return to the chief of the string, as you see the petticoat; and the strap, if it does not move from its place, then let it be, then leave it, then it will not aposteme or flesh out any other appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if it leaves, and addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of the bone that prick, if it can be; and if not, then it can be cut and drained; and the cure, as we have said, depending on how healthy it is.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the cheek broken unless it is set in its place when we put on the dressing or the arm; however, in the restoration made later, it does not click with the patient's pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And one should be sure that the cheek is restored in L jors, or at least a little less, according to the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the girl's joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the girl's joint there are few breaks, but it twists many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is not necessarily a fracture or a perforation, but it comes to all wounds and feels like a wound, and it is not well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put back what has been separated as much as possible, and then place the plaster, and put a round stone, if you have one, and tighten it as much as possible, then reward all the dispositions we have said for other fractures, such as aposteme chaut and other similar ones; and for every accident, if it comes to what is necessary, as much as it is possible to be healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the injury to the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "true" by right, not "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and all the breaking is like that of the arm, and therefore the restoration is done in the same way as that of the arm properly. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then it is felt with great pain and seen that it is well; then turn away.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	1. Therefore, extend it evenly, and place it perfectly aligned; however, it is necessary to ensure that the fracture is not severe, and if there are more pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And when you have completed your wound, if you have hair that is purple on one side and green on the other, and is long enough to reach from the knee to the ankle, then wrap it around the leg and tie it at the ankle, and lay it along the leg, and do not let the leg deviate to the right or left, and it is well; and no one has caused pain in the leg, and it was done with twine, and he puts it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly made it at the fracture or wound; and shake each leg every day to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure is as soon as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bones so much pain
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle never has a fracture, but the bones so much pain never have a fracture and you must put, and it only comes that it is bent in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones so much pain are fractured, and you see these bones overturning on one another, then put as many pillows as you can under the part that is on the ground, as if you were flying, and then now place your foot on the other side, until the bones come up; then press as much as they want to in their legs; then put the splint and stitch, and then sew the belly of the ankle with a small turn, then draw it towards the knee, then when you have covered the wound with bandages, and other things that you have knowledge of.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three or four days have passed, if the bone is not healed, you will find the bones unevenly split, broken, and dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are two broken bones, if they are repaired, as we have said, with the hand; then put a splint on one of the breaks according to the length of the bone, and make it wider than the other; then tie the joint that I have mentioned, and tighten the splint; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, if you put one on each according to its quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and tighten the joint around the peg; and make sure it is placed at the top of the socket, so that it stains well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other breaks, as soon as we have said them; and treat each accident in the same way that it comes.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone fracture of the little finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the woman's bone is broken, if it is made to fit, then it bends towards the side of the shoulder, and is held by the hand; then fill the nature of the cloth with the woman's bone, and put it as large as possible; then lower the woman's shoulder little by little, and gently, until the cotton comes out of the entrance of the nature, and returns the bone with the cloth; and when she sees blood, if the cotton is wet, and when she has bled, it is reinserted, and left in place for seven days or more: if the fracture is restored, and you see it, take a basin of water, and tie a string around the nipple, and blow all the water into the nature; then form the string in the nature, until the basin is empty: the nature will return to the fracture; then fill it with cloth, and leave it alone for several days, until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the elbow is broken, or of the woman, if it is restored as we have said in the elbow of the horse; and these fractures are not hidden that those who study and use it, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means in more directions the right way of restoration: understand the doubt.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the neck, when it is broken, take an goose's grip and bite the neck; then wrap the drapes around, and leave it three turns outside or inside, and it will be cured quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of a fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, just as it is large, if it is like the bone of the shoulder or elbow, or seems, that he is now healthy, if those wounds that we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the healthy wound is that it becomes inflamed, and you have nothing else, then resume to repair the fracture in the same hour, or the next day, if you do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if you do not come the next day, if you leave the restoration until the next day, as long as you are calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you will make the coming harm worse.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken, it should be set as soon as possible, so that you can place it gently in your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not easy to make with your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight feet long, and the length should correspond to the size of the wound; and for this reason, it is necessary to make three or four passes, according to the number of times you have to compress the break; and so it should be firm but not too tight, and it should be in front and large before, and then gradually reduce it behind:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palinche", because it is intended that the shoulders be placed on the head of the apparent bone; and the buckle once, as it rises, and be even on the other side.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is not clear, and the straps cannot well hold the bone, then it comes to pass that you cover the head of the bone with the strap, as long as the straps are in position.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you do not bring the bone back, as we have said, if you cover it with an instrument that is suitable for this, or cutting or sharp, then you should return to the bone that has been made rough and full of small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is realigned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it is suspected that there is something wrong with their natural joint.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you hang it long enough in its joint, then dip it in a piece of black, stiptique linen, and do it properly, as it should be; and do not put anything else on the wound or other parts that are oily, so that it does not cause putrefaction and corruption. Then dress the wound with appropriate medications after you have restored the bone, leave the wound exposed, cover it with a cloth according to the size of the wound, and make sure the wound is not stretched with the break; many times the patient has had this experience, and it has caused the patient to die or rot at least once; and the scars become softer and more glistening than the other scars.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that it will heal, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, but you cannot put on splints; then envelope the limb in cloth, in the limb of the splint, tie hard knots, and glue.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound is healing, and if everything goes well, and you put a salve on the wound, and if the salve is a safe remedy for wounds, and it looks like this.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to untie the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is swollen and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limb is aligned in a certain way that the bow can be easily passed.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to pass, and it cannot be held back but rather moves away from the bow, it has small pieces of bones, because it is necessary that you close the wound with a tent, and all these fragments that cause this pain, take them out.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess comes to the shoulder, or any other form of corruption, and it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed through the limb, if it is like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, or other similar bones of the large limbs, if it is not treated, because often death comes, but it is left as long as it bleeds; by chance it may heal after 20 days or 30, and then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, let it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of the cold things that come out of heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the joint, and it is even when it is near the joint, and it is a matter to see how the member is figured; and by chance, it cannot make the limbs its own nature.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If it is cold, then it is well: if it is treated with strengthening medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, and other similar things, if you do not take any of these things or all together, and mix them with warm wine, or with a large amount of urine, or with honey; and then apply them to the wound, and pull it out well, and do not let it slip from your hands; and then pull it out, and start another one, as long as the nodations are osteal; or you pull out a piece of plaster well made; for the property of the plaster is such that all the enflames in the limbs are converted into durtitude, and it becomes like a piercing when it is osteal, and it is painful to the bone, if the raseur is applied, and the superfluity is removed; or you leave it with no one, as long as it is osteal, and the cure as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A weak limb that is after the imprisonment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	After the fracture is restored, and weak after the weak members and subtle, if there are any causes: either because one was too tightly bound, and not as it should have been; or because it had too many ligatures, and could not come to the member; or because of multiple inflammations; or because of too great movements, not in its time; or because it has little blood in its body, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And if the cure is that you make the patient drink vinegar, and make the body tense as much as possible without multiplying in him; then give him warm water, and he will soon feel relieved; then put poultice on the member, if it attracts the great inflammation, and the swelling often turns green, until the inflammation reaches the member; and then restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The dislocated limb after the healing process
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after restoration, and the bone is openly broken, and the shape of the dislocated limb is deformed, it does not correspond to its natural form: if one does not believe the folk who say that the bone must be broken completely at once, and all others have done this in our land; and these bones are blamed, and great harm comes from it, and by chance the death occurs; however, if the swelling and pain are fresh, then it is necessary to raise them with hot water, or herbs that soften, if like spongy things, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and I apply a softening agent, as well as I can, and take the mucilage of spongy things, and cook with fat of linseed or olive oil, and apply; or take ripe figs, and crush with colon fiber, and similar medicines that dry the sweat.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is there where the node is held continuously and long with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be no movement in the limb at any hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awakened and made to hurt, as well as the incision, and it requires the forge at the bone, then cope with it as much as possible; make it smooth and light, and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, if it now comes to bring sense to the target.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we are late, and it is seen, and by chance it is reset to the shoulder; because it does not come to move the ear when it is swollen: many times sent pain and other pains are caused: always, when this happens, I make the patient healthier, then let him, as long as the abscess is closed, treat the limb with warm oil and oil, then gently reset the limb, and cure each member as it was cured in its shoulder.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the cauteries for the dislocations of the shoulder bones.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are two ways in which the mandibles are dislocated: either they are slightly crushed at their base, and become malleable; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and causing saliva to flow from the mouth that cannot be held, nor can the mouth be closed, and the tongue is wrapped around with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it returns through the more common positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it as soon as possible without force; and in such a way that the patient's hand teaches the surgeon how to open the mandible, and with the other hand hold the lower part of the dislocated mandible, which is divided into two parts; and the other two hands are deflected to make them equal; and instruct the patient to make the mandibles malleable, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And she measures it evenly, as it fits in her hand.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return it, then it is the second and third molars, as the arrows of hot and oily oil, until they are lightly returned; do not force too hard to return it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned evenly, and the patient's mouth feels very relaxed, if you apply soft, moistened cotton balls made of olive oil and wax to it, then gently press on the teeth; and the patient lies down on his back, and his head is between the knees, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor struggle too much, but chews gently on lean meat, as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jaws; and then take what you have gently pressed, and do not force your mouth open with your fingers and mouth, as long as the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaw bones cannot be set within an hour and are not converted to their original position, if fever and chills set in, and by chance solution comes from the stomach, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times have died those who came, in nine years.
de la forcelle	of force
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be removed from the cost, due to the continuation of the hand and the foot, and it is always dislocated at the end, and it is felt.

And the restoration is when the patient gazes at the masseter and extends his arms; then press on the palm of the hand, it will return; then place the splint and the bandage, and tighten; and the one who is towards the cheek cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is dislocated never, then reset it at the shoulder, as we have said; then place the splint and the bandage, and tighten, and command the patient to rest as soon as he is healthy; and then realign the head of the scapula, when it is released from the shoulder.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways for the shoulder to dislocate: either it dislocates at the acetabulum of the hip socket; or at the deltoid muscle; or by accident, at the acetabulum; and seldom, at the scapula, and not by the nerves; and more often towards the acetabulum, especially for those with little shoulder bone, because in this jump it is very hard; for those with enough shoulder bone, the jump is few, and returns to few.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by accident, it happens to some men with trauma or dislocation, and the shoulder is dislocated from an abscess, and make sure it is re-dislocated.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary therefore that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known the dislocations when they are towards the axle, and there is a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them clear diversity; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and then the axle at the bottom of the shoulder's head, just as if it were some other ones; and it cannot bring its hand to its neighbor, nor move any movements; and thus, if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you see it clearly at the axle; and this way of dislocation is not easily returned, when it is new, or if it is caused by a patient.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the physician gently places his hand on the patient's shoulder, then removes your hands from the joint, and gently relaxes it at the top of the arm; the physician gently places his hand, extends it upwards, and places it beside you; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands just now, if the physician should immerse the patient's shoulder in warm water; the physician gently softens and soothes it, like a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in warm water, and is soothing; then he places the patient's shoulder on his back, and places a bandage on the elbow properly, not too soft or too hard, and places the patient's foot on the bandage, and gently relaxes the shoulder muscle, and trains the physician's hand; and other physicians trace the shoulder muscle, if it does not move at all; this shoulder is now returned, and if you see that it follows in this manner: and that you face the larger shoulder; and it should be turned towards the chest, and bend the elbow away from the shoulder of the physician, and gently raise the elbow, if the shoulder hangs downwards; and other physicians train the physician's hand over the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then with him there is nothing heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is done in another way: and it is like this: and the bandage is made of long grass in the earth, whose ends are as a pin, and not too big or too rough; then it is put around the patient's neck, but if it has been braided enough, and the neck is too long and thin; then it is stretched out from one hand to another part, and the joint returns to its place quickly; and if it does not return in all these things that we have said, then this cure must be done: take two bands of one arm and four of the other, which have the ends inserted into the mouth so as to enter frontally from behind the ear, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie the head of the bone that was split, which was not broken by the patient, then place it in the cradle of the bone; and extend some of the arms over the long bone, and the helper over the shoulder, and the arm at the wrist of the hand, then put the arm on the shield of a wide shield, and extend the hands on the other side: the joint was now mended.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set, in whatever way that may be, if you happen to put the cradle of a spindle of even thread on one side, and then put the pasteur with incense and wool of oven all over the shoulder and the ribs, then tighten the cradle on the other side, and turn the lace on the pasteur, and wrap the hand around the arm, and let the hands remain in place.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	1. It is necessary that he drinks little, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it heals faster; then drink more after the fourth or seventh day, and move it; and if it is tight and not softened, it is healthy.

And if you do all this, and after seven days, the joint does not hold, and cannot raise the arm forward, then suspect that the nerve at the shoulder of the elbow is compressed or extended or softened; and suspect that the joint will never fit in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The first sentence to translate: "Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.

After the healing comes pain in the member, and then movement, if the patient uses hot water many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	The dislocation is expensive
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint that is expensive is repeatedly dislocated, and it returns to its original position; and it becomes dislocated in all directions, and even front and back, and the dislocation is not well replied because it can be seen and felt well; and it becomes dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the expensive remedy with the clean one, if you see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is thin, and cannot be shaved of the arm, nor touch its spine at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it always with the help of an assistant, because if it is not reset with the help of an assistant, it would be difficult to return; and by chance, it cannot be reset at all, even when it is in its place; rather than other dislocations, and it is more painful, and by chance it comes to death.

And the restoration is such that when it is in place, you can return it with your hand; and his arms are expanded, and his hands are held according to the course of the bone, from the top to the bottom, and he bends the joint at the root of his palm, as it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, then it returns when it doubles its hand on its hand, and proud of the root of the palm tree that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to the shoulder, then it is given a strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm in each part, then wrap a long and wide double strip around it; and when the patient touches the joint with the joint of his hand, if no oil can smooth the joint, then form the joints, as it re-emerges; and when it is at the shoulder, put a dry cloth with cow dung on it, and stretch it, and can the arm at the bottom of the patient's cheek, and leave some hairs, then let it go.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	When the joint is tight in its place, if it does not move, and is left alone; and if you see that the joint is not tight, then re-tighten the splint and the joint, and leave it for some time until it is firmly fixed; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the dislocation of the joint, and it becomes still, if he bathes and rubs gently, and presses until it is calmed; or you put on the joint a fat sheep's wool dressing, then leave it for one night and the bone, and let it enter a bath; and when it comes out, rub the joint thoroughly, then remove the wool dressing, and then enter or bathe twice or three times until it is healthy; and if you see, if you put on fat sheep's moistened and warmed with a brush, and pull it off; if it returns to its place.

des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the shoulder

And the sign is if the ankle is swollen, and before reaching the part where it is dislocated: the fingers are lighter, and it should be stretched gently with one's hands as soon as possible.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, if you can manage to sit with the affected leg straight, and tension the ankle with your hand, then pull the toe towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand, and then again with your right hand, and then pull it up, and gently push the toe up; and do this twice, as we have said, by stretching and pulling the toe up, and if it returns, that is good; but if not, if you continue the treatment, it will return; and if it cannot be returned, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and hold the knee firmly on the ground with both hands, and let the ankle hang loose; then trace the knee with your other hand, and stretch the toe out to your hands or to the other leg, where the knee is located; then stretch all the fingers equally, and the patient should hold it between the knees to keep the knee in place; then place the knee gently at the dislocation, and trace the healthy leg at the other end, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When the dislocation occurs, if it is immediately covered with plaster and poulticed, and the bandage is formed, and the leg is tied to the thigh, where the tendons are at the ankle joint, that the ligaments should not be too tight; then it is left for II to III days, and if the bandage is loosened, then the ligaments are relaxed; then the bandage is changed every IV days, and if it advances to the end of this term, it is not a mistake that the dislocation has not been corrected.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, if it is necessary to lance it, then it should be lanced, and as we have said before, as long as it is healthy.
des dois	Of two sorts, one is a dis
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are reset, if they can be extended well in the work, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no doubtful place on either side of the shoulder, then you must set it in the joint above or below, that is, straight. Then put your foot on the part where the joints open, and press firmly with your foot until it re-opens; and when it is equal, if it does not open, then place a table at the head of the shoulder, then form it, and leave it for three days, then remove it; and let it rest, as long as it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your treatment, whether you are skilled in the art and have not used it long, or whether you are merciful and compassionate and slow, do not be presumptuous; and at the beginning of things, use soothing remedies for the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to the bone immediately, unless the abscess has burst and is vomiting; and when the limb is at the bone, if it is swollen and inflamed, apply soothing remedies for the wound and cure it, as necessary, using desiccants; and if there is a break with dislocation, and the bones are sharp, if the bones break, then make them straight according to what we have said in simple diseases; and do not enter into a state of despair, according to what I have said, for this is good according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your heart.
